# Changelog

All notable changes to Hilt are documented in this file.

Format: [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/)

## [Unreleased]

### Changed

- **Library health is now authoritative, self-healing, and actionable** — Replaced the client-side badge recount with one backend issue contract whose `critical`, `warning`, and `working` meanings drive the summary, badge, and visible rows together. Ready artifacts with stale blocked queue sidecars are ignored immediately and removable through a fail-closed dry-run/`--write` reconciler. Individual source failures stay item-level warnings; Retry handles both resumable processing and legacy refetch exhaustion, while `Keep limited capture` or `Mark source unavailable` records a Hilt-local disposition, removes the exact terminal payload from the active queue before committing the decision, stops automatic retries, and keeps the item honestly unfetched/unscored. A mismatch or archive failure leaves the decision unsaved and the alert visible; a later healthy capture clears the old decision so any future regression requires a fresh review. Refetch prunes healed, deleted, archived, and acknowledged attempt records. The UI calls scheduled Connections work **Context enrichment** and treats it as blue working state. Recommendation runs now write sanitized structured receipts, later success supersedes retained stderr, Claude prompts travel over stdin instead of process arguments, scheduler logs are owner-only, transcript-only changes cannot trigger an editor run, and automatic cadence reserves at most one morning attempt plus one refresh attempt per New York day before model work. A seven-day cross-batch title guard prevents duplicate topics while preserving same-item resurfacing with new evidence. The shared task editor disables StarterKit's built-in Link extension before adding Hilt's configured Link extension, eliminating the duplicate-extension browser warning without changing link behavior.

- **Semantic graph retired, preserved as a time capsule, and replaced by deterministic Library Current fit** — Preserved the complete v1 source on published branch `archive/semantic-graph-v1`, annotated tag `archive/semantic-graph-v1-2026-07-18`, and a verified complete-history Git bundle; stored transactionally consistent, checksum/`quick_check`-verified `semantic.sqlite` and `graph.sqlite` snapshots, the 26-checkpoint/137-episode bake-off, model/configuration metadata, prompts/responses, and fidelity-labeled screenshots only in the private `${DATA_DIR}/archives/semantic-graph-v1-2026-07-18/` capsule. Live Hilt now calculates one full-corpus `explicit_context_hybrid` score map under configuration `s3` for Library lists, detail, archive, For You, and Briefing candidates: bounded BM25F current-work matching is combined with readable active Connections and attention judgments while Worth, substance, freshness, lifecycle, suppression, cooldowns, and the three-item Claude editor remain intact. Cards retain compact Worth; expanded evaluation now says `Worth = Current fit × Substance × Freshness`, explains matched targets/terms and each contribution, and separates immutable recommendation-time snapshots from current evaluation. Removed the semantic and knowledge-graph code, System Graph tab, graph links, route implementations, runners, schedules, databases, environment flags, dependencies, calibration/review tooling, and one-time bake-off runtime; retired API-family tombstones return `404`, stale graph links resolve to System Sessions, and unrelated Sessions and Map graphs remain. All model-backed Library summarization is pinned to `cli/claude/claude-sonnet-4-6`, Connections and recommendation editing are pinned to `claude-sonnet-4-6`, launcher jobs no longer import Gemini credentials, and static plus runtime tripwires reject Gemini model/endpoint use without affecting YouTube ingestion. TypeScript, focused hybrid/policy tests, the complete Library/Briefing/System suites, browser regression, production rebuild, and live tailnet smoke passed. Current evaluations report hybrid/s3; a first new editor batch remains separately approval-gated, so no live candidate packet was sent and no new batch was written during cutover.

- **EverCommerce calendar events now show attendees through Fantastical** — ICS remains the authoritative source for event time, recurrence, title, location, and cancellation state. An explicit foreground refresh normalizes Fantastical's protected local cache into a participant-only snapshot under `DATA_DIR`; after each successful EverCommerce feed refresh, Hilt matches that snapshot by Outlook UID and exact occurrence and fills missing organizer/attendee response data without replacing richer ICS fields. The supervised calendar worker never opens Fantastical's group-container database, avoiding macOS file-coordination/privacy stalls. Recurring series rosters enrich all expanded ICS occurrences, exact exceptions win when present, failures leave the ICS calendar usable, and provenance is recorded in each enriched row. Manual commands refresh the snapshot (`npm run calendar:refresh-fantastical`) or reapply it (`npm run calendar:enrich-fantastical`). Event detail replaces the former attendee count with a compact expandable roster and response-state labels. Unit coverage exercises series fallback, exact exceptions, ICS field preservation, and participant normalization; fixture E2E coverage opens the roster.

- **Meeting extraction workers now inherit Hilt's exact Node runtime** — The durable extraction coordinator invokes the repository-local `tsx` CLI with `process.execPath` instead of PATH-selected `npx`. This keeps native modules such as `better-sqlite3` on the supervisor's Node ABI even though the child PATH still prefers Homebrew for provider CLIs.

- **Post-meeting extraction now survives Hilt rebuilds instead of waiting for the nightly sweep** — Migrated trigger delivery from a JSON `fired_at` at-most-once marker plus an in-memory runner to schema-v3 `meeting_extraction_jobs` in the canonical per-vault SQLite ledger. Settled Granola meetings enqueue idempotently; a ws-server coordinator reconciles on startup and every 15 seconds, claims serial batches with renewable leases, and retries incomplete work with bounded exponential backoff. The detached extraction child renews the lease itself, so it may finish through a parent restart; if either process dies, the next coordinator reclaims the job and verifies canonical output before rerunning. Completion now requires the processed stamp, first-touch escalation state, and exact reciprocal proposal/task origins, not a child exit code. The 7:30 PM path discovers, enqueues, claims, and drains the same queue rather than bypassing it. A live vault proposal sink now fails closed unless `DATA_DIR` resolves the canonical SQLite marker/database, preventing repo-local ledger state from diverging from Bridge files. Meeting Ledger health reports queue depth, active jobs, oldest age, retry timing, failures, and the latest error; legacy health replies retain the same empty queue shape during migration, the Priorities launcher tolerates rolling upgrades, and the queue tuning knobs are documented in `.env.example`. The launcher shows active processing or terminal failure counts, and SIGTERM shuts the Granola host cleanly. Verification covers schema-v2 migration, dedupe, exclusive leases, renewal/expiry, retry/terminal state, restart-after-commit without rerun, file-first proposal reconciliation with the same task ID, the scheduled queue path, wrong-`DATA_DIR` refusal, all Granola/loop/task/briefing/API tests, TypeScript, and the isolated meeting-ledger E2E. Production was migrated from v2 to v3 without count loss, then a real settled CES meeting survived three pre-fix worker failures, was reclaimed after rebuild, completed on its persisted fourth attempt, wrote six entries and three reciprocal proposals, updated the active briefing, left queue depth and failed count at zero, and produced a verified 410-entry backup.

- **Recommendation validation failures repair themselves once and explain any remaining fault** — The Library editor still treats each recommendation batch atomically, but a model response with one or more deterministically rejected picks now gets one bounded same-run repair pass over the complete set instead of discarding all valid work and waiting an hour. The repair prompt receives the precise rejection reasons and must return a fully replacement batch that passes the original trigger, context-delta, resurfacing, similarity, limit, and duplicate checks. If the replacement still fails, health records the concrete per-pick reason rather than the generic `one or more picks failed validation`. The on-demand child supervisor now derives its default timeout from two complete editor-call budgets plus exit margin, so it cannot kill a legitimate repair under the former five-minute ceiling. A controlled live refresh selected five valid episodes from the current 80-item pool and cleared the pending warning; recommendation state remains Hilt-local rather than rewriting Library Markdown.

- **Library Health alerts now reconcile to visible diagnostic rows** — Replaced the dense reweave/intake/recommendation prose under the popover title with a compact Runtime analysis section for Recommendations, Dead letters, Intake, and Reweave. Recommendation model-validation failures now carry their own amber row, retry timing, and concise error instead of incrementing the toolbar warning badge from summary prose alone. Dead letters and blocked intake have the same explicit representation; Scheduler and Sources retain their per-row statuses. The toolbar badge now totals blocked plus warning issues rather than hiding warnings whenever a blocker also exists, and singular warning copy is grammatical. Active intake/reweave work stays blue/informational and does not inflate the alert count.

- **Reference Library warnings now age out and failures have a review lane** — Scheduler health now classifies stderr only when it belongs to the latest completed run, so append-only errors from an older run no longer pin `refetch` or recommendations in warning after a clean success; retained historical stderr remains inspectable but is not counted as a current notice. A quiet `Needs attention` lens now lives inside Admin filters under `Processing` and gathers terminal processing failures plus legacy source captures whose bounded refetch attempts are exhausted. It participates in the collapsed section's active dot and shared clear action without becoming another top-level browse dimension. The state is derived at read time from markdown processing/capture health and the existing Hilt-local refetch ledger, never stamped into reference files. Cards, list rows, and detail explain the failure in amber, while still-retrying and subsequently healed items stay out of the lane.

- **Briefings v2 completion roadmap refreshed against the durable-ledger release** — Re-audited the canonical remaining-work plan against pushed Hilt `4a4a983`, the live loop registry/APIs, current scheduler and retry paths, and the Bridge artifact worktree. Meeting's canonical SQLite ledger, verified backup/recovery stack, bounded repository, task joins, and read-only Ledger UI are now recorded as shipped foundations rather than an unfinished sandbox migration; Meeting phase graduation is narrowed to reports/verdict files and explicitly keeps SQLite under Hilt data. Unified conversations now count as the truthful base feedback path for Runtime and Goals, while premature Meeting calibration receipts and Briefing's missing scheduled feedback remain open. Durable Library recommendation cards are marked shipped, the Goals/Runtime race, manual-retry mismatch, weekend recovery gap, silent UI errors, server verdict-policy gap, surfacing dormancy, and artifact provenance remain prioritized, and same-disk disaster recovery for canonical operational data is newly explicit. Updated HOW-IT-WORKS, Architecture, and API references to the live proposal sink, Meeting storage boundary, native briefing failure receipts/retry behavior, bounded dismissed-history surface, and unified conversation store. Verification: live Meeting SQLite audit and task-ID reciprocal-join audit passed; 81 loop tests and 84 briefing tests passed. Documentation only; no runtime behavior or production rebuild.

- **Comments and chat now share one reusable, genuinely live conversation model** — Library detail has one comment action instead of competing comment/chat icons. Its Loft-style anchored popover starts as an asynchronous capture lane: comments post as queued messages and stay available for scheduled processing. `Chat now` expands that same popover into the durable conversation and starts the pending volley in place; the full Chats pane remains an optional expansion, not a forced navigation. Claude now runs with partial-message events, so prose arrives as text deltas instead of one completed wall, while a running thinking step and tool start/result transitions make the activity trace useful before the answer lands. The compact composer can queue the next volley during an active turn, explicit Stop still cancels, and closing the surface lets the request continue draining. An in-process per-thread guard prevents a reopened surface from starting an overlapping turn. The full pane retains the shared Loft-derived timeline: human messages are right-aligned Hilt-accent bubbles, assistant replies are unboxed reading-width prose, each run's trace is attached to the reply it explains, and source subtitles link back to navigable Hilt artifacts. Chats rows now protect title/preview width with a two-line, right-aligned metadata rail; visible state says `queued` rather than ambiguous `pending`, while Dev item, outcome, message count, and compact age remain scannable. Each turn still consumes only unhandled human messages, records a concrete outcome (`Answered`, `Changed files`, `Proposal created`, `Dev item`, calibration, or steering), and leaves the conversation open. Later comments reuse the same thread, attached chat, and Claude resume session; `Close conversation` is the only fork boundary. Scheduled consumers use the same per-message handling stamps, so feedback acted on immediately is not consumed again overnight. Verification covers parser deltas/tool lifecycles, overlapping-run rejection, thread/session reuse, per-message handling, queued attention, processor outcomes, Library adapters, shared conversation rendering, TypeScript, lint, and production compilation.

- **Priorities proposal hierarchy and alignment** — Moved Proposals immediately above To Do while preserving Notes as the leading weekly context section. `View ledger` now precedes the far-right collapse caret, matching the action edge used by Notes and To Do. Proposal decision markers use the task checkbox's responsive 16px/20px square, 1px border, and 3px radius with an amber dashed treatment, while meeting/thread metadata aligns with the proposal title column.

- **Priorities keeps decisions bounded while Meeting Ledger owns history** — Removed the unbounded `Dismissed · N` expansion from the Priorities proposal queue and attached a compact `View ledger` action to the Proposals header instead. Meeting Ledger now labels the former `Latent` lens as `Not surfaced`, explains every state in place, and defines sightings as later meetings referring to the same commitment. All proposal files are actionable regardless of origin: loop-backed proposals retain `/api/loops/verdicts` and its ledger audit, while feedback-thread proposals use a task-native verdict route with the same approve/assign/dismiss/revise controls and weekly-list promotion. Future thread proposals persist the processor analysis as their body plus a verbatim thread citation. Meeting-derived tasks now compose editable task notes with the complete live SQLite record in one stacked sidebar. The originating meeting remains an attachment card; the canonical `Meeting action` accordion contains summary, context, free-text due language, evidence, sightings, and record history; and ledger-linked tasks suppress redundant proposal/status and task-history presentation. New meeting proposals mint with blank notes, while proposed and accepted task titles/notes remain editable through the same non-lifecycle task patch route. A guarded exact-prefix migration removed copied ledger context from five accepted tasks and two proposals, retained all task audit History, preserved two already-empty tasks, and saved hashed pre-write copies under `DATA_DIR/task-body-migrations/`; its second pass found zero changes. The reciprocal `LedgerEntry.task_id` ↔ `TaskFile.origin.item_id` contract is part of `tasks:ids:audit`, and all nine current meeting-origin files still pass after cleanup. Two stale July 10 thread proposals created before this contract were removed recoverably after their underlying briefing and launchd issues were confirmed superseded/resolved.

- **Meeting actions now use a durable, scalable SQLite ledger** — Replaced runtime whole-file reads and rewrites of `ledger.json`, meeting summaries, and processed-meeting state with a canonical per-vault `better-sqlite3` store under `DATA_DIR`. WAL, `synchronous=FULL`, foreign keys, forward-only schema versions, transition guards, immutable before/after events, one-meeting transactions, a shared nightly/Granola writer lock, normalized extraction-run records, FTS5, fail-loud initialization, integrity checks, and a latched write block protect the ledger against concurrent or partial writes. An idempotent CLI supports dry-run, migration, parity audit, activation, readable export, verified backup, restore, and rollback; the untouched pre-migration JSON remains recoverable while generated compatibility exports become inspection-only. Successful writes create an integrity-checked `latest.sqlite`, 14 daily/12 monthly snapshots, and a live change marker. Extraction now separates complete-transcript observations from identity resolution; every resolver pass includes the full trailing 30 days, all older pending/accepted-open work, dismissal immunity, and older indexed matches, partitioning above a 40,000-token budget instead of truncating. Goals, briefing summary joins, recent report summaries, and the post-meeting trigger use bounded repository queries. Bridge Priorities adds a read-only, cursor-paginated Meeting Ledger pane with search, six mutually exclusive state lenses (including the exact latent pool), virtualized rows, full evidence/history detail, desktop/mobile layouts, WebSocket refresh, disconnected-only polling, and an explicit unavailable state when canonical health fails. New APIs expose list/detail/health without loading lifetime state. Storage verification proves exact 400-entry/119-latent legacy parity independently of model behavior, plus crash recovery, duplicate identity rejection, unsupported/corrupt database refusal, automated rollback/reactivation, a 40,000-row performance fixture, end-to-end post-meeting/verdict/restore behavior, and inspected desktop/mobile light/dark browser captures. The separate two-stage model pipeline was judged over the frozen 36-meeting corpus with Sonnet 4.6 extraction and Opus 4.8 judging: it scored `0.923` precision and `0.881` core recall with one suspected duplicate pair, versus the prior monolithic pipeline's `0.957` precision and `0.796` recall with two suspected pairs. This is a pipeline comparison, not a JSON-versus-SQLite storage comparison; the stricter prompt experiment was dropped rather than mixing optional extraction tuning into the migration.

- **Task identities survive proposal dismissal without reuse** — Task creation now reserves `t-YYYYMMDD-NNN` identities through a locked, atomically-written per-date high-water file at `tasks/.id-sequences.json`; deleting a dismissed proposal no longer makes its number available to a later task. The live vault was bootstrapped from current files, meeting-ledger stamps, briefing references, and Git history. Two pre-reservation July 7 collisions were repaired by retaining the first owners of `t-20260707-008` and `t-20260707-015` and remapping the later dismissed entries to `t-20260707-046` and `t-20260707-047`, including their loop report and historical briefing references. `npm run tasks:ids:audit` now fails on duplicate files or ledger stamps, outcome/file mismatches, a missing sequence file, or a high-water gap. The separate 119-entry June backfill pool remains untouched: those are un-escalated meeting observations, not missing proposal files.

- **Mobile briefing dates stay left-aligned on one line** — The selected briefing label now uses the compact yearless form below the `sm` breakpoint, keeps explicit left alignment, and cannot wrap away from its selector chevron. Desktop retains the year for historical context; the isolated Decisions E2E pins both forms.

- **Dismissed meeting proposals are inspectable and recoverable** — The active daily/weekend Decisions card now exposes every recent dismissal from each represented meeting, even when a regenerated briefing stamps only the remaining pending IDs. `Resolved` is reserved for accepted/completed stamped work; dismissals have their own quiet `Dismissed · N` disclosure with original copy, date/reason, and an undo icon. Restore recreates the original proposal file under the same task ID and provenance, appends a private restore action to the decision log, and reopens the meeting ledger on its next run without erasing dismissal history. The same recovery rows are available in Priorities and meeting detail. Historical briefings remain frozen to their stamped IDs. Verification covers persisted identity, pre-ledger undo, active/historical membership, immediate live counts, desktop/mobile layout, and isolated restore-through-UI behavior.

- **Decision previews keep their reading width under long meeting titles** — Replaced the fragile desktop pill/context/count grid with a stable metadata row followed by full-width editorial context. Long meeting pills now truncate without collapsing prose into a one-word column. The Decisions E2E now uses the real Listen360-length title and asserts row geometry at 1440px, the previously failing 987px viewport, and 393px mobile in addition to its live-state checks.

- **Scheduled For You runs get a realistic model window** — The 5:20 AM launchd pass was consistently terminated at the previous three-minute editor timeout even though the same validated batch completed when run with a longer window. The default is now ten minutes, still bounded well before the 6:00 AM briefing and still overrideable with `LIBRARY_EDITOR_TIMEOUT_MS`; stale-run recovery scales with that bound.

- **Work briefing recovery restores broad, file-native editorial discovery** — Removed the experimental six-project `work-projects` allowlist, its collector/analyzer, persisted fingerprints, 4:55 scheduler, generated Bridge artifacts, Work cardinality rules, and mapped-only Goals dependency. `Work & product` and `goals-areas` again synthesize broad observed git, agent, meeting, ledger, Library, project, roadmap, and delivery evidence. Bridge's hierarchy and actual activity define eligibility; a central project registry must not hide new or changing workstreams. Weekend refreshes no longer feed the target briefing's generated prose back into the model, preventing stale labels and conclusions from perpetuating themselves. The unified For You stream and redesigned Library briefing remain unchanged.

- **Decisions awaiting you keeps editorial context with canonical live state** — The briefing model again chooses and orders featured meetings and writes substantive meeting context from bounded meeting summaries. Its prompt receives exact allowed meeting citations and task IDs but not task titles; proposal-card copy, prior decision queues, and meeting-ledger inventory are removed from the editorial gather before synthesis. The composer preserves that prose and ordering, associates IDs with their canonical source meeting, appends omissions using stored meeting summaries, and rejects invented, duplicate, misplaced, or leaked proposal IDs without misclassifying ordinary accepted-task links elsewhere. The card header owns the live unresolved count; collapsed rows no longer concatenate task titles or repeat a body count. Meeting identity/count occupy a compact metadata row at every width, followed by full-width editorial context. Current daily/weekend briefings still absorb newly created proposals and broadcast `briefings-changed` after the atomic append so an open reader receives stored meeting context without navigation. Historical membership stays frozen, existing TaskCards/verdict controls remain live, resolved items stay behind `Resolved`, and legacy Next steps continue to render. The harness also restores a missing required H1 deterministically before validation, so sound editorial output is not discarded over boilerplate.

- **Docs frontmatter is collapsed by default with compact toolbar controls** — Markdown files now keep YAML metadata hidden until the toolbar's info icon is pressed, in both read and edit modes, and reset to the collapsed state when a new file opens. The former two-button Read/Edit segmented control is now one action icon: a pencil enters edit mode and a book returns to read mode, freeing toolbar space without changing unsaved-edit protection.

- **Manual Editor's Memo runs keep the local weekend anchor** — The memo filename now derives from the machine's local calendar date instead of UTC. A Saturday-evening rerun can cross midnight UTC; previously that produced a Sunday-dated memo that the exact Saturday briefing selector correctly ignored. Scheduled 5:30 AM runs were unaffected, but manual recovery now writes the same Saturday artifact the weekend briefing expects.

- **Library recommendations now have one coherent copy system and briefing hierarchy** — Pipeline `v2.6` makes artifact descriptions strictly evergreen and source-centric, while recommendation episodes own the contextual reason to pay attention; editor validation rejects pitches at `>=0.65` description similarity and context-triggered pitches that do not reflect their supplied non-artifact evidence. For You and Briefing cards now render the pitch as their sole unlabeled description, Recent/New/Search render only the source description with a quiet active-recommendation sparkle, and detail separates a dated recommendation callout from the normal source digest. `rec=<episode-id>` preserves frozen briefing/resurface pitches without recording passive impressions; the reader holds that exact context blank while it loads and falls back to the current episode only after the historical ID is known unavailable. `Library & knowledge` now renders three explicit modules: an editorial recommendation lead plus cards and attached `View all`, a prominent Saturday-anchored weekly memo band, and a quiet exact-date health footer with `Daily library report` or an honest unavailable state. The memo scheduler moves to Saturday 5:30 AM. Historical briefings and existing markdown remain compatible. Verification: Library 188 passed / 3 existing skips, Briefing 58 passed, thread/comment 53 passed, TypeScript clean, isolated three-day recommendation E2E green with 24 inspected desktop/mobile light/dark captures, production rebuild green, 9/9 launchd jobs loaded, non-publishing live weekend shadow valid with the published briefing hash unchanged, and the real For You/Recent surfaces rendered without console errors.

- **For You and the daily briefing now share one durable recommendation stream** — Replaced the expiring eight-item score cache with immutable per-vault recommendation batches, a latest-episode-per-artifact feed projection, recommendation verdicts, and persisted refresh/backoff state under `DATA_DIR`. The 5:20 AM editor considers fresh ready saves/candidates plus older items only when novel 72-hour meeting/task/project/area/briefing evidence creates a real reason to revisit them; trigger fingerprints, materially changed pitches, 7/14/30-day exposure/read/dismissal cooldowns, duplicate suppression, and strict all-or-nothing model validation prevent repetitive resurfacing. The existing WebSocket server can start one on-demand editor child for meaningful new signals without adding an idle daemon. For You is now a cursor-paginated infinite feed: a new episode updates and moves the same stable card, `Why now` is distinct from the source summary, read state never reorders items, impressions record only visible episodes, and dismissal/comment/Undo affect recommendation state without changing saved/candidate lifecycle. Live insertions preserve deep-scroll anchors behind the quiet new-items control. Briefings freeze up to three new unread episode IDs as `rec:<episode-id>` placements, passively hydrate compact Library cards, and open the real artifact in native For You only on click; later batches cannot rewrite that morning. Health exposes the last batch, pending refresh, backoff, and errors. Scoring config is now `s2`. Verification: 179 Library assertions passed (3 existing skips), 51 Briefing tests, 53 thread/comment tests, TypeScript clean, and the isolated three-day Playwright scenario passed repeatedly across desktop/mobile light/dark with exact order, resurfacing, dismissal feedback/undo, live insertion, anchor preservation, stable read ordering, native navigation, and mobile action-clearance checks.

- **Unified recommendation rollout verified on the real vault** — Reinstalled all nine Library launchd jobs and confirmed the editor at 5:20 AM, then ran one controlled `s2` morning pass: seven complete episodes were atomically selected from an 80-item pool, health cleared pending/error state, the durable feed grew from the seven bootstrapped legacy episodes to 14 cards, and the Bridge Library worktree did not change. The production For You page rendered the new batch cleanly with no page errors. A non-publishing weekend shadow briefing then froze the top three new unread episodes and passed validation at 5.1 KB with no warnings; network-substituting only the shadow markdown into the production Briefing renderer confirmed hydrated recommendation cards, long-copy clamping, saved/candidate/read states, and `View all` before `Daily library report`. That smoke test also hardened two CLI contracts: the standalone briefing recommendation formatter now defaults to `~/.hilt/data`, and weekend generation explicitly requires the H1 already enforced by the validator and used by existing briefings.

- **Briefing recommendations now read as real Library cards** — Featured items in the `Library & knowledge` section use compact inset cards with stable thumbnails, provenance, lifecycle/read state, and the existing comment/dismiss actions. The editor-written episode pitch is now the card's unlabeled description; the similar artifact summary is omitted in this compact briefing context instead of repeating the same idea twice. Dismissed, unavailable, and loading placements retain the same inset-card geometry so the section does not jump between states.

- **Briefings v2 completion roadmap — cleanup before expansion (2026-07-10)** — Added a source-audited canonical roadmap that separates production cleanup and unfinished v2 contract work from meaningful enhancements and genuinely new capabilities, preserves the full remaining-work inventory, and orders it behind explicit definition-of-done gates. Linked the historical implementation plan, phase log, launch report, and living HOW-IT-WORKS reference to the new current source of truth. Documentation only; no runtime behavior changed.

- **Thin saved pages now recover and transcribe their primary embedded video** — Some product posts expose only a tagline in normal extraction while the substantive source is a native player. The Library now applies a cost-gated fallback after normal capture: study-mode explicit saves with thin prose inspect `<video>`/`<source>`, iframe, social metadata, known providers, and serialized Vimeo directives; muted loops and videos under 20 seconds are ignored; captions are preferred and audio is downloaded/transcribed only when necessary. Successful recovery makes the timestamped transcript canonical Raw Content, persists page/player/provider/method provenance, embeds Vimeo/direct video in the reader, and sends the transcript through the normal digest/reweave/eval path. Failed required video capture uses the existing two-attempt policy. Short timestamped transcripts can no longer masquerade as a digest when summarization fails, and a failed manual reweave no longer checks off Connections. The live Notion Ship OS item recovered its 63-second Vimeo captions under the same stable UID and was repaired into a source-grounded five-stage workflow note. Its automatic Claude reweave was blocked after capture by the account's current monthly spend cap, so the final note uses the recovered transcript plus previously validated vault targets; that external failure did not affect the new capture path. Pipeline iteration `v2.5`; prior v2 variants remain current-compatible. Verification: TypeScript clean, Library `155` passed / `3` existing skips, deterministic captions and no-captions/audio paths green, production rebuild successful, supervised app/WS healthy, and the live reader shows the Vimeo player, digest, links, and worth score.

- **Library reweaves use native structured output instead of prompt-only JSON** — The live Notion Ship OS save completed its full Claude vault exploration and produced a useful digest plus five proposed connections, but one quoted phrase inside `digest_markdown` was not JSON-escaped. `parseReweaveOutput` therefore discarded the entire otherwise-complete result, the readable L1 digest became `ready` with `reweave_pending`, and the score correctly remained hidden while newer valid responses completed. Reweave calls now pass an explicit JSON Schema to Claude and prefer the returned `structured_output` object; a regression proves quoted prose round-trips. The same stable Notion artifact was reweaved through the repaired path, cleared pending, gained three accepted connections, and now evaluates at worth `0.268` (`27` in the UI). Pipeline iteration `v2.4`; prior v2 variants remain current-compatible because the content contract and digest voice are unchanged.

- **Chats becomes a top-level view — threads and chat sessions unify; System returns to pure monitoring (Justin, 2026-07-10)** — Justin: chats "shouldn't be buried in the systems tab"; accepted design: *unify rather than relocate* — a conversation is ONE concept, whether anchored to an object (feedback thread: comments + agent replies + processor transcripts) or free-standing (chat session from a Library item or the API). New top-level **Chats** nav entry between Docs and System (`MessagesSquare`, URL `/chats`, deep link `/chats/<id>` where the id may be a thread id or chat id — both stores probed, thread wins ties; `"chats"` joins `VIEW_PREFIXES`, `ViewMode`, and the WS `/navigate` validViews). `src/components/chats/ChatsView.tsx` merges the former `system/SystemThreadsView.tsx` + `system/ChatsView.tsx` (both DELETED): one recency-sorted list where thread rows render as the Threads index rows did (target icon/label, snippet, resolution story + 24h blue dot, Dev item chip, working pulse fed by sending attached chats, hover Process) and free-chat rows as the Chats rows did (kind icon, title + unread "9+" badge, contextLabel, preview, status column, ⋮ archive/rename/mark-unread menu with suppression) — paddings reconciled (shared px-3, border-l-2 selection) so the merged list reads as one family. **De-dupe invariant**: a chat session whose id appears in ANY thread's `chat_ids` renders inside that thread's drawer, never as a free row. **Lenses** replace Open/Resolved/All: *Needs you* (open threads incl. dev items + chats sending or unread — archived-with-attention included) / *All* / *Done* (resolved threads + archived chats), defaulting to Needs you when non-empty else All; kind filter tabs carry over and apply within the lens (thread targets map into the chat kind space — briefing kinds → Briefings). Right pane dispatches by shape: thread → `ThreadDrawer`, chat → `ChatPanel` (`autoMarkRead={false}` + suppression-aware mark-read); split persistence keeps the `hilt-chats-split` key; Process-all stays in the toolbar with cancel + n/total progress. Merge/lens/de-dupe logic is pure and tested (`src/components/chats/conversations.ts` + 12 vitest cases). **System cleanup**: `SystemMode` drops `threads`/`chats` (Sessions/Apps/Stack/Sync/Performance/Graph remain — monitor-first); legacy `/system/threads/*` and `/system/chats/*` URLs redirect to `/chats/*` via `legacyConversationScopeFromSystemUrl` (Board effect), so stale briefing/doc links keep working; stale `hilt-system-mode` localStorage self-heals through the `isSystemMode` guard. HOW-IT-WORKS gains a top-level "Chats — every conversation, one tab" section (flywheel pointers updated); CLAUDE.md navigation views list adds `chats`. Keyboard shortcuts renumbered end-to-end: ⌘6 Chats / ⌘7 System in NavBar's `VIEW_KEYS` handler and the double-⌘ shortcuts popup, matching ViewToggle's advertised 6/7 (review fix — the initial pass renumbered only ViewToggle's labels, leaving ⌘6 on System and ⌘7 dead). Suites: system 17, chats/threads/chat/stream vitests 91, pinned vitest 74 green; tsc clean.
- **Chat v1 W2 — shared `ChatPanel` + Library artifact chat entry point (2026-07-10)** — `src/components/chat/ChatPanel.tsx` promotes ChatsView's in-file `ChatSessionPane` composition (header · `ChatMessageList` · `ChatComposer` over `useChat`) into the shared chat surface: `{chatId}` opens an existing session, `{context, contextLabel}` is first-turn mode (the server creates the session on first send; context rides along only until a chatId exists), `headerActions` slot for host affordances (e.g. "New chat") plus optional close X, files-touched chips resolve to Docs via an `onOpenFile` override or the default `workingFolder` join (absolute outside-vault paths pass through — ChatsView idiom), and unread ownership: by default the panel PATCHes `{unreadCount: 0}` whenever the open session shows unread — covering mark-read on open AND on turn-complete-while-open — while `autoMarkRead={false}` leaves suppression-aware hosts authoritative. `ChatsView` performs the promised swap: in-file `ChatSessionPane` deleted, both split/mobile sites render `ChatPanel` with `autoMarkRead={false}` so the manual-unread nuance keeps living in the list. **Library entry point**: `LibraryArtifactDetailPane` grows a `MessageCircle` "Chat about this reference" action in the top icon row (deliberately distinct from the `MessageSquare` comment trigger); it opens the chat as a house right-drawer over the detail pane — absolute overlay in the pane region, `lg:` 30rem right drawer keeping the artifact visible, full-bleed on mobile, no backdrop, no entrance animation. Reuse-vs-new: the click queries `GET /api/chat/sessions` (updatedAt desc) and reopens the most recent non-archived `{kind:"library", id: artifact.id}` chat; the drawer header's `Plus` starts fresh via a nonce-keyed remount. The vault root for files-touched chips is recovered from `abs_path` minus the vault-relative `path`, so Library needs no workingFolder threading. Edge-case ledger rows carried: concurrent-send guard (useChat `statusRef`), Stop → partial persisted + idle + no error toast (abort-aware error suppression), empty-output fallback (server-side "Claude returned no text."), unread bump-then-clear on turn completion.
- **Supervised rebuilds now deploy WebSocket/background-service code** — The live Library acceptance test exposed that Mercury's `ws-server` had remained alive since July 7: `npm run rebuild` swapped only Next.js, so the newly shipped intake daemon never started (`last_polled_at: null`, no foreground Library subscription) until the WebSocket child was restarted manually. The headless supervisor now reloads ws-server on every successful rebuild stamp (alongside app-server in prod, ws-server only while Next remains in dev), and switch-to-prod reloads it explicitly after absorbing its own stamp. The recovered live Raindrop save, `Introducing GPT-Live`, was discovered on the immediate foreground poll, rendered in Recent, reached `ready` in about five seconds, and the following one-minute poll completed cleanly.

- **Open threads gain a manual Resolve control (Justin, 2026-07-10)** — the drawer's action row pairs Process with a quiet Resolve button (PATCH `resolveAction: "closed"`) so dev items — and any open thread Justin is done with — have a way OUT of the Open queue. The resolve API existed with no UI caller (W3 verify note). Resolution story renders "Closed · <time>"; summaries/pills/transcripts refresh on the shared keys.


- **Dev-item processing keeps Hilt software feedback open for Justin's pass** — Thread processing now has a third outcome alongside processed edits and proposal minting: a final-line `DEVITEM: <diagnosis>` marker is stripped into a normal diagnosis reply, stamped as `dev_item`, and traced as "Dev item diagnosed" in the saved processor chat. Loop-mapped dev threads still get `processed` so they leave the guidance set, but `markProcessed` now preserves OPEN status when `dev_item` is present and the processor does not resolve them. System → Threads shows a quiet amber "Dev item" chip, and the drawer status line reads `Dev item · diagnosed …` while keeping the normal Process affordance for Justin's later dev pass.
- **W4 — Library items get the universal comment experience (library unification, 2026-07-10)** — `LibraryArtifactDetailPane` drops its bespoke feedback UI (hand-rolled comment list + textarea POSTing to `/api/library/[id]/feedback`) for the shared W1 pieces: a count-pilled `CommentPopover` trigger anchored at `{kind:"library", id}` sits first in the top action-row icon cluster (with the copy-link/copy-reference/graph icons — Justin's "comment button with the share and copy and link icons" placement), and the eval panel's Feedback block is now the shared `ThreadView` (edit/delete + resolution story built in; renders nothing when empty). Composer lives in the header popover — the MeetingEntry pattern (popover = quick layer, ThreadView = durable record, same SWR key so they cannot disagree). Same data either way: library comments have been thread-backed since C2 (`library-feedback.ts` adapts over the thread store), so existing threads render unchanged; `feedback_left` still emits for library targets in POST `/api/threads`, and the `/api/library/[id]/feedback` route adapters stay for API compatibility — only the pane's private UI dies.
- **Calendar adds the shared Family Google calendar as a first-class source** — Hilt Calendar now has a `family` source (`family02812820750125202686@group.calendar.google.com`) alongside Personal, Priceless, EverCommerce, and US Holidays, and the source picker orders them Personal → Family → Priceless → EverCommerce → US Holidays while preserving the existing duplicate-resolution priorities. It uses its own `HILT_CALENDAR_ICS_FAMILY_URL` because Google secondary calendars have separate iCal feed URLs even when they are visible in the same Google account; fixture sync now includes school-calendar events such as first day/no-school days, and the setup docs call out the per-calendar URL requirement.
- **W3 — resolved threads say how they resolved (consumption legibility)** — System → Threads resolved rows, the ThreadDrawer header, and the under-object ThreadView outcome line now render the resolution story via a shared `resolutionStory` helper (`threadTargetHelpers.ts`) — "Calibrated · meeting-actions", "Processed", "Proposal minted", "Clustered" (unknown actions humanize) — instead of a bare "Resolved · <raw-action>" plus a redundant "processed" chip; ThreadView collapses its up-to-two stamp lines into one caption under the agent reply, so the reply reads as the outcome. Rows resolved in the last 24h carry the small blue "new since you looked" dot (the ViewToggle/Library unread idiom), making overnight feedback consumption visible at a glance under Resolved/All. Presentation only — no store or API changes.
- **W2 — threads become a chat client in System → Threads** — Ported the reusable chat transcript pieces from Loft into `src/components/chat/`: `ChatMessageList` renders chat/user/assistant turns and live drafts, `ChatTracePanel` renders Claude tool/step evidence per assistant message, `ChatComposer`/`useChat` own normal chat turns, and `stream.ts` centralizes NDJSON parsing plus trace-event merging. Feedback threads now join to processor chat sessions through `Thread.chat_ids` / `ThreadSummary.chat_ids`: the processor appends the newly minted chat id immediately after emitting `{type:"session", chatId}`, so the running transcript is discoverable while the Claude turn is still streaming. System rows now open a right-side `ThreadDrawer` instead of navigating directly: the drawer header owns cheap target jumps, the body renders the shared `ThreadBlock`, saved processor chat transcripts with traces, a live streaming processor turn, the drawer-owned Process affordance, and the same Enter/Shift+Enter comment composer semantics as `CommentPopover`. Thread rows read like chat sessions: whole-row click opens the drawer, selected rows get the quiet blue tint, working rows show the emerald pulse from either local processing, process-all progress, or a sending chat session. Process all is cancelable and reports per-thread progress using the existing batch `thread-start` event.
- **Live Library intake and progressive processing** — Explicit saves now become useful markdown placeholders before enrichment, backed by stable `artifact_uid` identity and a crash-resumable per-vault queue. The existing WebSocket server adaptively polls explicit-save sources immediately on Library activation, every 60 seconds in the foreground, and every five minutes in the background; provider backoff persists in source state and the scheduled ingest remains a fallback. One on-demand serial child advances metadata → capture/transcription → digest → reweave, exits when idle, treats a readable digest as ready even with `reweave_pending`, and leaves exhausted captures in a terminal `Needs source` state with Retry. A dedicated watcher broadcasts saved/candidate/queue changes; Feed/List/detail SWR state updates in place with a five-second fallback only while disconnected. Toolbar and mobile pull-to-refresh use fast intake without reload, processing cards reserve media space and respect reduced motion, active items pin only in Recent/New, deep-scroll insertions preserve the first visible card behind an `N new items` control, and processing items cannot be marked read or scored. Health now reports daemon cadence, queue depth, active item, blocked count, and oldest queued work. Final hardening preserved an `add` event across rapid placeholder-enrichment writes, delayed scroll-anchor restoration until the new stable ID actually enters SWR, prevented transient virtualizer scrolls from dismissing the `N new items` notice, and resets canceled mobile pull gestures. The detail pane now keeps the static `Ready · Connections pending` checkpoint visible until reweave completes. Verification: Library 146 passed / 3 existing skips, watcher 2/2, TypeScript clean, isolated desktop/mobile Playwright green with ready + blocked/Retry fixtures, mobile media/overlap assertions, deep-scroll anchoring, and disconnected-WebSocket fallback; the separate live OpenAI fetch reached upstream but returned HTTP 403.
- **Library candidate promotion now preserves completed reweaves** — Explicitly saving a URL that already exists as a discovery candidate now promotes the candidate as-is when it already has a completed study reweave: free-form digest body, `connection_suggestions`, `connection_reasoning`, `reconnected_at`, `reweave_candidates`, `attention_judgment`, and YouTube preflight metadata are carried into the saved reference. This fixes the YouTube bookmark path where a strong auto-discovered transcript digest could be downgraded to legacy Summary/Key Points during promotion.

- **Unfeatured ⏭ Next-steps meeting groups render the shared TaskCard interior (Justin, 2026-07-07)** — `MeetingGroupCard` (EscalationsPanel) previously kept old-style `LoopItemRow` interiors while the featured lane rendered TaskCards — the same ask had two styles side by side, and unfeatured proposals could not be opened ("why does the same content have two styles"). Verdicts post through the same `/api/loops/verdicts` wire as the featured lane (decided items render read-only badges; dismissed items are filtered before bucketing, as before). `LoopItemRow` survives inside group cards only for non-ask items, wrapped in its own list. Suites: briefing 40, vitest 74 green; tsc clean.
- **Briefing sections gain a per-section expand-all / collapse-all header control (Justin, 2026-07-07)** — Each briefing section card's header now carries a single right-aligned icon button: lucide `ChevronsUpDown` (expand all) that becomes `ChevronsDownUp` (collapse all) after clicking — NOT a plus (plus suggests adding something). The icon reflects the NEXT action and flips only on its own clicks; local child toggles never move it (it is an action toggle, not a computed all-state). **Mechanism**: a per-section `ExpandSignal { version, expanded }` broadcast (type + `useExpandSignal` hook exported from `MeetingCard.tsx`) — `BriefingContent` mints a fresh signal object per click; children apply it in a `useEffect` keyed on the signal object (identity = version), so repeated clicks re-apply even if the reader toggled a child locally in between, while every child keeps its own local open state and click toggling exactly as before (signal + local state — deliberately NOT lifted state). **Coverage**: `CollapsibleItem` detail expansion, featured ⏭ `MeetingCard` entries (`NextStepsMeetingItem`), and the section's `EscalationsBlock` — standalone `LoopItemRow` detail, `MeetingGroupRow` shells + their nested ask rows, and unfeatured `MeetingGroupCard` shells + rows. Deliberately excluded: the per-meeting "Dismissed · N" tails, popovers, and the `EscalationsFallbackFold` (not a briefing section; usually empty). All-prose sections (nothing expandable) and the Sources section render no button — no dead control. Signals reset when the briefing content changes (section indices are per-briefing). Styling: h-4 w-4, tertiary → primary on hover, "Expand all"/"Collapse all" title tooltips, soft/rigid haptics matching the row toggles. Suites: briefing 40, vitest 74 green; tsc clean.

- **Proposal-card cleanup: dotted-square checkbox + verdict dropdown on the card; blockquote + full meeting card in the pane (Justin, 2026-07-07)** — The proposal TaskCard loses its two space-eaters: the tiny italic provenance quote (moved to the pane) and the hover-reveal verdict button row (Justin hated the reserved empty space). **Card**: a decidable card now shows only title + dated meeting pill (+ existing badges), and leads with a **dotted-square checkbox** — the bridge-checkbox position/size (h-4 w-4, leading slot, items-start row), but lucide `SquareDashed` in amber, echoing the Library candidate `CircleDashed` as a square: "not yet a real task". Read-only cards (landed tasks, `showStatus`) unchanged. **Pane** (`TaskFilePanel`): the quote renders in the BODY as a full-size `<blockquote>` above the editor, styled as the house `.bridge-task-editor` blockquote (3px `--border-strong` left rule, `pl-4`, text-sm/1.6, tertiary) — not tiny italic. The meeting linkage graduates from a badge-row pill to a **full `MeetingObjectCard`** in its own pinned-attachment section (the same slot/weight BridgeTaskPanel gives project cards), resolved via the same `useObjectCard` hook + `ObjectCard` dispatch the pill popover uses so the card data can't drift; title click navigates via the resolver nav (`useScope().navigateTo`); a failed resolve degrades to the pill. The pane's verdict buttons move into a `VerdictActionMenu` kebab in the header (BridgeTaskPanel's slot); the note field renders in its old section when opened from the menu; the status badge stays. `VerdictNoteTrigger` remains for EscalationsPanel (ask rows deliberately untouched).
