### Fixed

- **One decision, one badge: "Accepted" → "Approved" (Justin, 2026-07-10)** — the verdict badge (live escalation lane, emerald "Approved") and the task-file status badge (file lane, gray "Accepted") are the same approve click seen from two data paths; cards migrate lanes as ledger stamps land, so the badge appeared to change meaning. `STATUS_BADGES["accepted-me"]` now reads "Approved" in the same emerald tint; `accepted-agent`'s chip likewise unifies to "Assigned to agent". Follow-up (same day): the badge SLOT unified too — the verdict badge used to render below the card text while the status badge sat inline-right of the title, so the same decision wrapped differently card-to-card; TaskCard now has one inline badge slot (verdict wins as the fresher signal when both apply). Display-only — statuses, files, and behavior unchanged.


- **First-touch extraction always escalates (Justin, 2026-07-10)** — an ask extracted THIS RUN reaches the verdict queue (and mints its proposal) even when its meeting has aged past the 3-day recency window, so a days-late first extraction (trigger + nightly both failed for a stretch) can never park work ledger-only and invisible. The backfill flood-gate still holds for entries opened by prior runs that never met the recency bar. Live-fired both sides in an isolated ledger-home: a May 8 meeting first-touched on July 10 escalated + minted; the stripped-stamp control run stayed latent.


- **X Articles now ingest their real title/body before digest and connections** — The live Chamath acceptance save appeared promptly and streamed stage checks correctly, but X bookmark intake had requested `note_tweet` without the newer `article` field. The artifact therefore stayed titled `Article shared by Chamath Palihapitiya`, cached only a 138-character t.co wrapper, and spent two long Claude passes weaving plausible connections around content it had never captured. X intake now batch-enriches article bookmarks through authenticated `tweet.fields=article`, and per-item retry fetches the same field so already-queued saves recover without changing UID/path; `article.title` and `article.plain_text` become the canonical source. Capture health now gates reweave, so wrappers cannot check off Connections or consume Claude time, retry cooldowns start when an attempt fails rather than when it began, and explicit Retry clears the prior run's completed-stage checklist before starting again. X Article recovery no longer emits the contradictory metadata-limited source note, and feed descriptions truncate at sentence/word boundaries instead of mid-word. Pipeline `v2.3` changes capture integrity only; v2/v2.1/v2.2 remain current-compatible.

- **Live intake no longer re-promotes old YouTube candidates every minute or scores an unfinished weave** — The first real Raindrop acceptance save exposed two distinct failures. First, foreground window polling found the hidden `promoted` candidate records for Adam Mosseri and Why Domain Experts Are Winning and called fast promotion again on every 60-second pass, minting `-2` through `-12` durable copies and repeatedly moving the old videos to the top of Recent. Intake now checks durable/archived URLs first and only promotes a candidate whose status is not already `promoted`; a regression runs two repeated window polls and proves one durable file, zero promotions, and duplicate reports. The 22 generated copies were backed up and removed, the strong original files retained and stamped with their stable IDs, and candidate provenance retargeted to the originals. Second, the launchd supervisor PATH omitted `~/.local/bin`, so the on-demand worker could not find Claude and silently degraded new study saves to `reweave_pending` L1 digests in about five seconds. The wrapper and binary resolver now find the local Claude install. Pending study items show a static `Ready · Connections pending` state and are excluded from eval/For You until a successful weave clears the flag and completes the processing timeline. A real repair pass then reweaved GPT-Live into five notes (worth 2→40) and the hiring tweet into three notes with a proper title (worth 0→13).

- **Dismissed proposal ids no longer render as dead raw-token chips in briefing bullets (Justin, 2026-07-10)** — The ⏭ FFTC/FWD Intersections MeetingCard said "Dismissed · 6" but its expansion still showed the stamped ids (`t-20260707-001`, …) as inert chips: dismiss deletes the proposal FILE, and once the loop stamps its ledger the item also leaves the escalations feed — so the id became UNKNOWN and the never-drop rule (built for out-of-band file deletions) kept the raw token. Verdict-dismissals are IN-BAND: the ledger remembers the minted `task_id` (`/api/loops/dismissed` already returns it), and the id's representation is the "Dismissed · N" tail. **Mechanism**: `BriefingContent` now builds `canvas.dismissedTaskIds` from the dismissed-ledger records' `task_id` merged with limbo dismissals still in the escalations feed; the sub-line strip decision is extracted into pure helpers in `canvas.ts` — `isConsumedTaskId(id, knownIds, dismissedIds)` and `stampedIdLineDisposition(line, isConsumed) → "drop" | "strip" | "keep"` — applied in BOTH paths: `NextStepsMeetingItem`'s leftoverLines and `CollapsibleItem`'s detail lines (whose `hasDetailTasks` routing and headline token strip now also count dismissed ids, so a fully-dismissed ask list no longer leaks raw tokens through the plain-markdown branch). A consumed id strips exactly like a live known id; the Dismissed tail keeps counting by LEDGER id (untouched); an id that is unknown AND undismissed still keeps its inert chip — never-drop preserved for genuine out-of-band deletions, locked by 6 new predicate tests. Suites: briefing 46, vitest 74 green; tsc clean.
- **goals-areas analysis call: tolerant JSON extraction + retry + honest failure notes (W5, 2026-07-09)** — The loop's daily Claude alignment call started failing when the model got chattier (prose before/around the JSON; sometimes fenced). New pure helper `extractJsonObject` (src/lib/loops/extract-json.ts): fenced-block first, then largest balanced-brace candidate (string/escape-aware), then whole-text — valid non-object answers correctly return null instead of plucking inner objects (adversarial fix: fenced top-level arrays). On null, ONE retry with a firm "Return ONLY the JSON object" suffix. Health notes now distinguish `analysis parse failed (after retry)` from call failure/rate-limit, and the catch logs the error (a silent catch hid a timeout for a full diagnostic session). Default `LOOP_GOALS_TIMEOUT_MS` raised 240s → 600s (live measurements: the call now runs 5-8 min; a 540s-budget run succeeded at 7m57s and wrote a healthy artifact over the failed one). 8 new extract-json tests; loops 66/66.


- **Calendar overlap warning badge no longer pushes timed events down the week grid** — Events flagged with the amber EverCommerce-coverage warning (`hilt-calendar-event-unblocked`) accidentally overrode ScheduleX's required absolute positioning with `position: relative` so the `!` badge had a local positioning context. Warned overlapping events then flowed after the previous event's height before applying their `top` offset, which made Friday's 3:00 PM Weapons Camp events render around 5:30/7:00 even though their event text still said 3:00. The warning style now leaves ScheduleX positioning intact; the timed event is already positioned, so the badge still anchors correctly.
- **HUD no longer hides meetings that start inside the current meeting block** — The HUD used the current meeting's end time as the floor for both the Next card and the Today agenda. That made a short overlapping meeting like `Priceless weekly admin` (1:45–2:00) disappear while `Design review` (1:30–2:00) was current, even though the full Calendar grid rendered it correctly. The HUD agenda selector now skips only events that have actually ended, excludes the current event itself, and lets later-starting overlaps surface before the next clean handoff. Covered by `hud-agenda.test.ts` with the exact current/overlap/next shape.
- **Task-body wikilinks no longer open a second Electron window** — Following the same `[[projects/...]]` task-body wikilink now stays in the current Hilt window. Tiptap's link extension defaulted rendered anchors to `target="_blank"`, so Electron could open an extra internal BrowserWindow even while the task editor's click handler navigated the existing app to Docs. `BridgeTaskEditor` now removes the default target from task links and intercepts wikilinks during capture (`mousedown` + `click`) before native new-window handling can run; external HTTP(S) links still open externally via the existing click path.
- **Task-body wikilinks to Bridge root folders open the real file from task panes** — The task editor previously resolved every slash-bearing wikilink relative to the task file, so `[[projects/seb-1on1-strategy/...]]` inside `tasks/t-20260707-026.md` opened Docs on the nonexistent `tasks/projects/...` path and showed "File not found." `BridgeTaskEditor` now routes known Bridge root folders (`projects/`, `meetings/`, `areas/`, `tasks/`, etc.) through the vault root while keeping explicit `./` / `../` links and task-local `media/` attachments relative to the task file. The save path keeps root-relative wikilinks as `projects/...` instead of rewriting them to `../projects/...`; covered by `task-editor-links.test.ts`.

### Added

- **Chat v1 W3 — System → Chats workspace (design-level port of Loft's `AIEditWorkspace`, 2026-07-10)** — New `"chats"` System mode (`MessagesSquare` icon — Threads owns `MessageSquare`) rendering `src/components/system/ChatsView.tsx`: a resizable split workspace, chat list left / open chat right, split ratio persisted to localStorage `"hilt-chats-split"` clamped [0.28, 0.72] (default 0.38) via the Loft pointer-capture drag (persist on pointerup only). **List**: filter tabs by context kind (All + only the kinds present, each with a quiet count — library/doc/person/task/meeting/loop-item/briefing-line/none map to Library/Docs/People/Tasks/Meetings/Loops/Briefings/Other); attention-first grouping (**Active** = sending or unread — archived-with-attention included, Loft semantics; then **Open** by `updatedAt` desc; then an **Archived** collapsible group paginated 20/page, reset on collapse). **Rows carry the full Loft metadata set**: context-kind icon, title + unread badge capped "9+", contextLabel subtitle, preview line (last snippet, or emerald "Claude is working" while running), right column with compact time-ago (`Now/5m/2h/1d`) and status label+icon (Running emerald pulse / Unread blue / Archived / Open), selected-row blue border+tint, hover-revealed `MoreVertical` context menu (mark read / **mark unread** / rename inline — no modal / archive-unarchive; Escape + outside-pointerdown close). **Unread suppression ported** (Loft `suppressAutoReadPathRef`): a manually-marked-unread chat stays unread — the auto-read effect (which PATCHes `{unreadCount: 0}` on open and on turn-complete-while-open) skips it until the row is explicitly clicked or marked read. **Right pane** composes the shared W2 primitives (`useChat` + `ChatMessageList` + `ChatComposer`) keyed by chatId (remount aborts in-flight streams on switch — ThreadDrawer invariant); files-touched chips open in Docs via `workingFolder`-joined `navigateTo("docs", …)`; sends resume the stored `claudeSessionId` server-side. Kept in-file until the shared `ChatPanel` lands (one-line swap). **Deep link**: `/system` scopePath `/chats/<id>` follows the Graph remainder pattern (`Board.tsx` `graphScopePath` generalized to `systemSubScopePath`); row clicks stay internal state (v1 contract). Data via SWR on `GET /api/chat/sessions` (focus revalidate + 15s poll + mutate after every PATCH/turn). Mobile: full-width list, selected chat as inset overlay (SystemThreadsView pattern). No route changes. Suites: system 16, chat lib+stream 26 green; tsc clean.
- **Universal comment experience — ONE floating CommentPopover everywhere (v3 W1, Justin's top design ask)** — Commenting is now one identical experience at every trigger: a `MessageSquare` icon button that opens a FLOATING composer anchored at the trigger (the house `ObjectPopover` shell — portal, fixed-position + viewport clamp, outside-mousedown + Escape dismissal), sitting on top of the canvas instead of an inline box pushing content around. The popover shows the target's thread history compact (the shared `ThreadBlock` rows exported from `ThreadView` — edit/delete hover affordances and the quiet Process action work inside the popover) above a textarea composer (Enter = send, Shift+Enter = newline, posts via `postComment`); posting keeps the popover OPEN showing the new message (Figma behavior); an empty thread shows just the composer. **Count pills**: the trigger badges the target's total message count (incl. agent replies) once a thread exists, fed by new `src/hooks/useThreadCounts.ts` — ONE app-wide SWR fetch of `GET /api/threads` summaries on the same `"/api/threads"` key SystemThreadsView polls, looked up by the pure `targetKey`, which is EXTRACTED to client-safe `src/lib/threads/target-key.ts` (no fs imports; the store re-exports it — parity pinned in `threads.test.ts`). `mutateThreadsForTarget` now revalidates the summaries key alongside the per-target transcript key, so pills, popovers, under-body ThreadViews, and the System Threads index all refresh on the one mutate path posts already use. **Placements**: meeting header — the trigger sits immediately left of the kebab (the bottom-of-notes labeled CommentBox composer is removed; the under-body ThreadView Comments section stays as the record); task pane header — trigger left of the verdict kebab, under-body ThreadView kept (popover = quick layer, section = full record, same anchor + SWR key so they cannot disagree); briefing bullets (`ItemFeedbackButton`), escalation ask rows, and the whole-briefing button replace their inline-expanding CommentBox forms with the popover — hover-reveal stays the bullet idiom, but a nonzero count pill FORCES trigger visibility (the action-cluster wrappers in `BriefingContent`/`MeetingCard` stop hover-gating the whole cluster; the copy button self-gates instead). Escalation rows now anchor read AND write on the loop-item target (postComment already routed task targets to their origin loop-item; the popover's history/count must land on the same thread). `CommentBox` survives only as the inline primitive inside `VerdictNoteField` (TaskCard's verdict-riding note is a different gesture — untouched). Adversarial-review fix: `AskVerdictControls` (EscalationsPanel) now calls `mutateThreadsForTarget` on the loop-item anchor after a note-riding verdict and passes `onPosted` to its `VerdictNoteField`, so notes posted through the briefing-lane verdict controls refresh the row's count pill and any open popover on the same mutate path (previously only TaskFilePanel's verdict/note paths did). Suites: threads vitest 28 green (3 new targetKey parity tests); briefing 40, pinned vitest 74 green; tsc clean.
- **System Threads UI can process open feedback threads (v3 unit C3 UI)** — Added a System → Threads inspection mode backed by `GET /api/threads`: local Open/Resolved/All filters, quiet open/resolved counts, SWR stale-while-refresh polling, hover-revealed per-row Process actions, and a toolbar Process all action over open threads. The view stays inside the shared System secondary toolbar/list idiom, links only task and library targets for now, and drains the existing NDJSON processor streams through the new browser client. Open under-object `ThreadView` blocks also gain the same quiet Process affordance; resolved threads remain read-only.

- **The feedback flywheel — comment threads become calibration receipts or processed edits/proposals (v3 unit C3 backend)** — A comment thread is no longer a dead end; it travels one of two roads. **Calibration (passive)**: new shared pass `runThreadHealthPass` (`src/lib/loops/health-pass.ts`) — on each node run it sweeps the node's OPEN, unreplied comment threads (scoped by `loopIdsForHome`, the same registry resolution the loops feedback store uses), and for each one posts an agent reply (`agent:<loopId>` · "Consumed as calibration guidance for the `<loopId>` run `<date>`."), stamps `processed`, and resolves `{ action: "calibrated" }` — a *visible record* of consumption that replaces the old silent `markFeedbackProcessed`. Feedback still rides the extractor prompt as guidance exactly as before; `markFeedbackProcessed` stays intact for other callers. A `renderFeedbackHandledSection` helper renders a `## Feedback handled` artifact block (empty summary → nothing). Wired into all three shadow-node runners: `scripts/loop-meeting-actions.ts` Phase 0b (replacing its bare stamp), and — newly — `scripts/loop-runtime.ts` and `scripts/loop-goals-areas.ts` (which had no feedback pass; their domains' threads now ride the same flywheel). The library node's version is `recordClusteredFeedback` (`src/lib/library/library-feedback.ts`): `scripts/library-steering.ts` now posts `agent:library` · "Clustered into the steering report `<date>`." + resolution `{ action: "clustered" }` on every clustered thread (best-effort; `processed_at` stays owned by `/process-library-feedback`). Agent replies are filtered out of `getStoredComments`/`listStoredFeedback` so the loop never re-clusters its own note. **Processing (active)**: `processThread` (`src/lib/threads/processor.ts`) runs ONE Claude turn (Read/Edit/Write/Grep/Glob/LS — no Bash; the `runClaude` call is injectable for tests) over a preamble built from the thread's C1 context ref + messages, persists it as a NORMAL chat session (streaming the same `session`/`trace`/`message`/`complete`/`error` NDJSON events as `/api/chat/message`), posts the final text back as an agent reply, and resolves the thread. If the reply's last line is `PROPOSAL: <title>`, it mints a proposal task into `$VAULT/tasks/.proposals/` with `origin.thread` set, strips the marker, appends `Minted proposal <id>.`, and resolves `{ action: "proposal-minted" }`; a Claude failure leaves the thread OPEN for retry. Endpoints: `POST /api/threads/[id]/process` (404 unknown / 409 resolved, then NDJSON) and `POST /api/threads/process-all` (`{status?: "open"}` — serialized, hard cap 10, no parallel spawns; per-thread + summary events). No Thread-shape change (`origin.thread` already existed on `TaskOrigin`). Suites: new `src/lib/loops/health-pass.test.ts` 6 (node:test) + `src/lib/threads/processor.test.ts` 12 (vitest) green; loops 58, threads/chat vitest 59 green; runner smoke tests write only the shadow sandbox; tsc clean.

- **Threads render under their objects — ThreadView + task-pane & meeting comments (v3 unit C2 UI)** — New `src/components/threads/ThreadView.tsx`: read-only rendering of every thread anchored to ONE `CommentTarget` — dense message rows (author chip: "You" for justin, the loop name for `agent:<loop>`; time-ago via the shared `formatRelativeDate`), quiet tertiary `Resolved · <action> · <time-ago>` / `Processed · <time-ago>` metadata lines per thread, and hover-revealed edit/delete on justin-authored messages (inline edit → `PATCH /api/threads/[id]` `{messageId, text}`; trash → `DELETE /api/threads/[id]/messages/[messageId]` — deleting the last message deletes the thread and the section simply disappears; no confirm, single-comment delete is not "truly destructive"). Empty/loading/error states render NOTHING — no shell; the section only exists once a comment does. Data via `GET /api/threads?target=` through SWR keyed on the exported `threadsUrlForTarget(target)`; posting surfaces refresh with the exported `mutateThreadsForTarget(target)` (global SWR mutate on the same key — no refresh-callback prop-threading). **Task pane** (`TaskFilePanel.tsx`): a "Comments" section under body/History (the History-section header idiom) anchored to the pane's existing `commentTarget` (origin loop-item when one exists, else the task id — the SAME routing `postComment` uses, so posts land exactly where the pane reads); `VerdictNoteField`'s pure-comment Send wires `onPosted` → thread mutate, and verdict success also mutates (a note riding a verdict lands in the thread store through the loops feedback adapter). **Meeting view** (`MeetingEntry.tsx`): the `meeting` kind activates in UI — a quiet Comments section at the bottom of the Notes tab (below the Next steps / My Notes / AI Notes accordions): `ThreadView` + the labeled `CommentBox` ("Comment" — the whole-object idiom, per the compact-vs-labeled split), anchored at `{kind:"meeting", rel}` via the existing `meetingVaultRelPath` (transcript-only meetings have no Notes tab and no comment affordance — accepted). Briefing bullets deliberately get NO inline ThreadView (canvas stays clean; the System threads index next unit owns discovery), and there is NO Process-now affordance yet (next unit). Suites: threads 25, pinned vitest 74 green; tsc clean.

- **Comments become THREADS — one store, one write API (v3 unit C2 backend)** — The two comment stores collapse into a single thread store: one JSON per thread at `DATA_DIR/threads/<uuid>.json` (`src/lib/threads/{types,store}.ts` — chat-store discipline: atomic temp+rename, normalize-on-read never throws, UUID ids validated before every path join). A `Thread` anchors to the comment primitive's `CommentTarget` verbatim and carries messages (`author: justin | claude-sim | agent:<loop>`), an open/resolved status, the loops `processed` stamp (stamping resolves — consumed feedback is a closed conversation), an optional `resolution`, and `source_ref` (migration provenance = idempotency key). **Append-to-open semantics**: a new comment on a target with an open thread APPENDS; resolved targets start fresh threads; target identity is kind+ids (`targetKey` — `loop-item.artifactDate` and `anchor.citation` deliberately excluded). **Write API**: `POST /api/threads` (create-or-append, 400 on malformed targets, emits `feedback_left` for library targets), `GET /api/threads` (summaries; `?target=` returns full transcripts), `PATCH /api/threads/[id]` (resolve or edit-message), `DELETE /api/threads/[id]/messages/[messageId]` (last message deleted → thread file deleted). **Adapters, signatures unchanged**: the four loops feedback fns (`src/lib/loops/stores.ts`) still speak `FeedbackRecord` — message id = record id; home→loop-id resolution via the registry (`loopIdsForHome`: sibling `registry.yml` first, env-vault fallback for shadow homes, domain "briefings" ↔ loop id "briefing" pinned) — so `scripts/loop-meeting-actions.ts` consumes feedback unmodified; the library feedback fns (`src/lib/library/library-feedback.ts`) still speak `LibraryComment` — steering/workbench/metrics and the library routes work unmodified; `/api/loops/feedback` and the library feedback routes keep their exact contracts (handlers untouched). **postComment** routes ALL kinds to `POST /api/threads` (`ImplementedCommentTarget` widens to the full union — library + meeting activate); task comments land on the origin loop-item when one exists, else thread under the task id — the automatic task-file note-line dual-write is RETIRED (threads are the visible record; existing note lines untouched). **Migration** `scripts/threads-migrate.ts` (dry-run default, `--write`, idempotent via source_ref/message ids): one thread per legacy record from every vault + shadow `feedback/records.jsonl` (processed records arrive resolved with an `agent:<loop>` consumption message) and one per library comment; source files left in place as history. Level mapping: item+anchor → briefing-anchor (the anchor kind carries no loop id — non-briefing anchors collapse to the briefing loop on read-back, one processed live record affected), item+item_id → loop-item, section → briefing-section, briefing → briefing (dateless legacy records borrow the created_at day). Amendment to the normative `loops.test.ts` feedback test (the only sanctioned edit — flagged in-file): homes must now resolve via a registry and same-target comments merge into one thread, so the fixture seeds a registry + distinct item ids; assertion intent unchanged. Suites: new `src/lib/threads/threads.test.ts` 25 green (vitest, not in the pinned `test:vitest` list — package.json untouchable this round); loops 52, library 136, pinned vitest 74 green; tsc clean.

- **Chat v1 backend — chat lib + streaming route + session routes (Workstream 1 of docs/plans/chat-v1-implementation-plan.md)** — Content-anchored Claude CLI chats, ported from Loft's chat system. **Lib** (`src/lib/chat/`): `types.ts` — `ChatContextRef` extended past the plan's library/doc/person/none with the v3 phase-C kinds `task`/`meeting`/`loop-item`/`briefing-line`; trace/message/session/stream-event types; Loft-exact `deterministicTitle` (7 words / 58 chars). `run-claude.ts` — per-turn `claude -p --output-format stream-json [--resume]` spawn with line-buffered stdout parse + trailing-partial-line flush, `session_id` capture from any event incl. `result`, AbortSignal→child SIGTERM, `buildClaudeSpawnEnv` (overlays `~/.claude/settings.json` env, blanks `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`), binary discovery `~/.local/bin/claude` → `/usr/local/bin/claude` → PATH; single exported constants `CHAT_ALLOWED_TOOLS='Read,Edit,Write,Grep,Glob,LS'` (no Bash in v1) and `CHAT_MODEL='sonnet'`; `summarizeToolInput` keeps persisted traces small — full tool inputs never stored. `store.ts` — one JSON per chat under `DATA_DIR/chat-sessions/` (app state, NEVER the vault; same DATA_DIR resolution as the library stores), atomic temp+rename via the shared `atomicWriteFile`, normalize-on-read so schema drift or a hand-corrupted file degrades instead of crashing the list, UUID id validation before any path.join (traversal guard). `context.ts` — `buildFirstTurnPrompt`: library fully hydrated via `getLibraryArtifact` (title/url/path/summary + content head ~12k), task via `readTask` (title/status/body), meeting reads the vault note head; doc/person/loop-item/briefing-line are labeled stubs for later workstreams; every kind yields a sane `contextLabel`. **Routes**: `POST /api/chat/message` streams NDJSON (`session` → `trace`/`message` → `complete`|`error`) and persists SERVER-SIDE as the run progresses (divergence from Loft's client persistence — kills the last-write-wins race, survives panel closes mid-stream); turn-1 CLI prompt = context block + user prompt but the STORED user message is the prompt alone; retry-without-resume (non-zero exit, no text, had a resume id) emits a warning trace and reruns fresh; abort (client Stop) SIGTERMs the child and persists the partial transcript with NO error event; empty-output success persists "Claude returned no text."; `filesTouched` collected vault-relative from Edit/Write/MultiEdit inputs; unread bumps on turn completion. `GET /api/chat/sessions` (summaries: counts + ≤120-char snippet, updatedAt desc), `GET`/`PATCH /api/chat/sessions/[id]` (full session; archivedAt/unreadCount/title). No UI yet — ChatPanel and System → Chats are Workstreams 2–3. Suites: new vitest spec `src/lib/chat/chat.test.ts` 22 green; library 136 green (untouched); tsc clean.

- **Meeting-extractor `context` field: proposals carry the surrounding discussion (v3 follow-up, Justin-approved)** — A minted proposal carried only title + provenance quote, so verdicts were decided without the discussion that produced the ask. The extractor (prompt v2.2 — additive, not extraction tuning) now emits `context` per commitment AND per sighting: the transcript-grounded surrounding discussion — what was being discussed and why the commitment arose — sized to the DECISION rather than a length rule (Justin, 2026-07-08: usually a couple of sentences, a short paragraph when the commitment emerged from a longer back-and-forth or carries conditions; omitted when the discussion gives nothing beyond the quote). The runner validates it defensively (`cleanExtractedContext` in `meeting-ledger.ts`: string-only, whitespace-flattened, capped at 1500 chars — a runaway-model guard, not an editorial limit; invalid/missing is never an error), stamps it on newly OPENED `LedgerEntry.context`, and fills it on identity-matched existing entries that lack one via `fillContextIfEmpty` (never overwrites — forward-only enrichment; covers both the explicit-sighting path and the dismissed-immunity backstop fold). `mintProposalFromLedgerEntry` writes the context into the proposal BODY as its own leading paragraph (stated-due line follows after a blank line); entries without context — all 358 production entries at ship time — mint byte-identical bodies (pinned by test). Live-fired isolated (`--ledger-home` + `DATA_DIR` override into a scratch sandbox) on one gold-set meeting to verify the extractor emits context end-to-end. Suites: loops 52 green (6 new: clean/fill semantics, context-less ledger round-trip, prompt contract pin, mint with/without context); tsc clean.

- **Revise retired; the comment is the correction (Justin, 2026-07-07 evening)** — For a pending ask, Revise and a comment were the same gesture with accidental plumbing differences, and the split created a real trap (Enter in the note field posted a comment while the user believed they revised — adversarial finding). The Revise button is gone from every surface: three decisions (Approve / Assign to agent / Dismiss) plus ONE note gesture — type a note and click a verdict to attach it, or Send it alone as a comment. Comments on task-backed asks DUAL-WRITE: the loop's feedback drawer (extractor guidance) AND a visible note-line in the task file (the visibility Revise used to provide; C2 lifts these into threads). Also fixed from the round's review: the escalation-row comment form no longer fades on blur (persists open, wraps to its own line); digest truncation is surrogate-safe and newline-flattened; /api/loops/feedback gained its first in-tree contract tests (item/section/anchor + the artifact_date enrichment, declared deliberate).

- **The comment primitive — ONE "leave a comment" gesture, pre-built ahead of Phase C (Justin, 2026-07-07 evening — approved)** — The verdict-note input is deliberately NOT a one-off: it is the same gesture as the briefing feedback buttons, built once, because C2's threads absorb exactly these comments ("a comment is the first message of a chat session with a deferred agent turn"). **Target model** (`src/lib/comments/types.ts`): `CommentTarget` — a typed union over task / loop-item / briefing / briefing-section / briefing-anchor / library / meeting; **this union is the anchor contract C2's thread store adopts verbatim** (documented per-kind semantics + backing store). `library`/`meeting` are typed OUT of `ImplementedCommentTarget` until C2 (compile-time excluded; runtime throw through a cast). **Router** (`src/lib/comments/post.ts`): `postComment(target, text)` — storage stays in today's stores behind this one function: briefing/loop kinds → `POST /api/loops/feedback` (faithful FeedbackTarget translation — per-bullet anchors now also carry `artifact_date` when the surface knows the date); `task` → the origin loop item when one exists (a task comment IS feedback on its source ask), else a `- <iso> note: <text>` line appended to the task-file body via PUT `/api/tasks/[id]` (the file is the record; C2 lifts these into threads). **UI** (`src/components/comments/CommentBox.tsx`): one component replaces the three bespoke inputs — `ItemFeedbackButton` (briefing bullets + MeetingCard actions), `BriefingFeedbackButton` (whole-briefing, labeled form), and the EscalationsPanel `LoopItemRow` feedback form (which adopts the per-bullet icon→inline-input→check-flash interaction; classes copied, zero visual drift elsewhere). `FeedbackTarget` gains `section?: string` (valid only at `level: "section"`) so the `briefing-section` kind round-trips; the feedback route validates + stores it.

- **Verdict + note unification: any verdict can carry the why; a note alone is a pure comment** — In TaskCard, TaskFilePanel, and AskVerdictControls the revise-only input is replaced by ONE shared implementation (`src/components/comments/VerdictNoteField.tsx`: `useVerdictNote` control + `VerdictNoteTrigger` icon in the verdict-button row + `VerdictNoteField` input). Typing a note and clicking ANY verdict posts `{verdict, note}` in the single `POST /api/loops/verdicts` request — exactly as revise did. A note with NO verdict click, submitted via the field's own Send, posts through `postComment` to the item (pure comment, no decision) — this replaces what Revise semantically was, but the **Revise button stays** (posts `verdict: revise` + note; with no note typed it opens the field, preserving today's muscle memory; C2 retires it into threads per the plan). **Ledger + extractor**: the loop's pass 0 already persists `entry.verdict = { verdict, at, note? }` (type + apply site verified — no change needed; new round-trip test locks it); A7's `dismissedLedgerDigest` lines now carry the reason when present — `ma-… · justin · action — declined: <note ≤100 chars>` — so the extractor learns WHY an ask was declined (rides the existing RECENTLY DISMISSED prompt section; no prompt/extractor change). Tests: ledger note round-trip, digest with/without/blank/truncated note, verdicts-route note-on-dismiss record. Suites: loops 46, tasks 85, briefing 40, vitest 71 green; tsc clean.

- **Tasks are clickable everywhere — the task pane is file-id addressable (Justin, 2026-07-07 evening)** — Clicking any TaskCard (Proposals section, briefing canvas, meeting Next steps, the object popover's task card) opens the task detail pane: title, status badge, dated meeting pill, provenance quote, body, and History — with the full verdict button set in-pane for proposals. On Priorities it opens natively; from any other view a `hilt:open-task` event (the calendar-deeplink idiom, `src/lib/tasks/deeplink.ts`) switches to Priorities and opens it. Because the pane reads the task FILE directly (new `TaskFilePanel`), done/dropped/past-week tasks open read-only with no weekly row required, and a bogus id degrades to a quiet "Task not found" pane. Build note: the round's agents were killed mid-report by API errors — the work was complete and green; verification was performed by hand (suites + live click-journey QA: proposal click → pane; cross-view dispatch → view switch + pane; not-found pane).

### Added

- **Click any task, anywhere → task detail pane (file-addressable pane + universal task-open channel)** — Justin's expectation: clicking ANY task — proposal or accepted, on any surface — opens the task detail sidebar; on Priorities natively, from other views by switching to Priorities first; a done/dropped/past-week task still opens. **Pane** (`src/components/bridge/TaskFilePanel.tsx`, new): the FILE-addressable sibling of BridgeTaskPanel — keyed to a task-file id (`t-…`), all data via `useTaskFile` → `/api/tasks/[id]`, no weekly row required. Accepted/in-progress: title + body editable (PUT); the `## History` audit section splits out of the editor and renders read-only (pure split/join helpers in `src/lib/tasks/task-body.ts`, node-test spec `task-body.test.ts` incl. a round-trip against `applyStatusTransition`'s actual output). Proposed: read-only fields + the SAME verdict buttons as ProposalsSection (POST `/api/loops/verdicts` via origin); the pane stays open after a verdict — approve refetches into Accepted, dismiss shows a Dismissed badge over the last-known content (the file is gone; SWR's stale data is the memory). Done/dropped: read-only. Provenance quote, meeting ObjectPill, due badge, status badge included. **Selection model** (`BridgeView.tsx`): weekly-positional selection (`selectedTask`) gains a mutually-exclusive file-id selection (`selectedFileTaskId`); `openTaskByFileId(id)` prefers the weekly row (full BridgeTaskPanel via `taskIdFromTaskPath` match) and falls back to the file pane; both desktop side-panel and the mobile bottom sheet render either pane. The `openTaskRequest` consumer now waits for the weekly list and accepts BOTH id shapes (weekly `task-N` and file `t-…`). **Open channel** (`src/lib/tasks/deeplink.ts`, new): `requestTaskOpen(taskId)` dispatches `hilt:open-task` (the calendar-deeplink idiom); Board listens, switches Bridge to Priorities, and forwards the id as the existing BridgeTaskOpenRequest (`openBridgeTaskFromHud` generalized to `openBridgeTask`). The CLI/WS navigate API accepts a task deep-link: `{view:"bridge", path:"/task/t-…"}`. **Surfaces wired**: `TaskCard` gains a pure `onOpen?: () => void` prop (card body click + hover chevron affordance, BridgeTaskItem's idiom; verdict buttons/revise form stop propagation) — passed by ProposalsSection (native open, no view switch), briefing canvas `CanvasTaskCard` + briefing MeetingCard next-step cards (`BriefingContent.tsx`), meeting Next steps real task files (`MeetingEntry.tsx`; synthetic unminted asks stay open-less), and `ObjectPill` task refs (popover click-through AND coarse-pointer tap route through `requestTaskOpen` — the B5 resolver's `{view:"bridge", scope:""}` stays as-is). Exported `DueBadge`/`STATUS_BADGES`/`VERDICT_BUTTONS`/verdict badge helpers from TaskCard so the pane speaks the identical visual language.

- **Recycle orphan sweep: active-but-unlisted task files now ride into the new week (`carryUnlisted`)** — The gap: an ACTIVE task file (`accepted-me` / `accepted-agent` / `in-progress`) with no line on the weekly list is invisible everywhere except its origin meeting, and because the recycle carries LINES, it would never ride into future weeks (orphan sources: mirror-failure adds/approvals, hand-deleted lines, pre-splice-era approvals; live count at ship time: zero — preventive). **API** (`src/app/api/bridge/recycle/route.ts`): POST body gains optional `carryUnlisted?: string[]` (task FILE ids). Per-id server-side validation, defense-in-depth against the client's identical computation: `isValidTaskId` (path-traversal gate), file exists in `tasks/` (never `.proposals/`), status ∈ {accepted-me, accepted-agent, in-progress}, not already linked in the OUTGOING list, not already carried by the normal carry set (the retry-guard prior-mint relink case). Every valid orphan gets a v2 line rendered from its FILE — a RELINK/line-render, never a re-mint (one identity per unit of work): `accepted-me`/`in-progress` append after the carried task block in `## Tasks`; `accepted-agent` splices into the "Ready for agents" section via `insertWeeklyV2LineInSection` (created when missing) — the same home the verdict mirror uses (`AGENT_SECTION_HEADING` moved to `src/lib/bridge/weekly-v2-view.ts` so both write into one section). Invalid/stale ids skip with a warn and are reported (`carriedUnlisted: n`, `skippedUnlisted: [{id, reason}]`) — an orphan never fails the recycle. A5 rerun guards unchanged. **Modal** (`RecycleModal.tsx`): an "Unlisted tasks" group beneath the normal carry list when orphans exist — computed client-side (`useTasksList` active task files minus ids linked on the current weekly via `taskIdFromTaskPath`), checkbox per orphan DEFAULT CHECKED (exclusion-set state so late-arriving SWR data stays pre-selected), one-line muted explainer; no orphans → no group. `useBridgeWeekly.recycle` passes the ids through. 8 new route tests (placement per status, exclusion, skip reporting for dropped/done/proposal/missing ids, no-duplicate vs outgoing-link and vs retry-guard prior mints, traversal rejection, v1-outgoing sweep).

- **B5 display follow-ups (Justin's live-briefing review): heading-grade pills in bold context + unfeatured ⏭ meeting groups take the MeetingCard shell** — Two fixes. **(1) Heading-grade pills** (`globals.css`): a pill inside `strong`/`b` now matches the 🧠 bold leads exactly — `font-size: 1em` (default stays 0.92em), `color: var(--text-primary)`, weight 600 (shipped earlier today) — "if they're used in place of where there would otherwise be a normal heading, they should look like headings, just with a pill wrapping". The date segment stays metadata: tertiary/400 AND one step smaller (`0.92em` of the now-1em pill) — the plain-text form it replaces rendered dates as text-xs tertiary, and the size step keeps the label/date hierarchy inside the chip. Selector list includes `.dark strong …` (0,3,0) because `.dark .hilt-object-pill` (0,2,0) sets a translucent-zinc color that would otherwise beat the 0,1,1 strong rule; `var(--text-primary)` resolves per theme so one declaration serves both. `line-height` stays 1.4 (1.4em < the row's leading-relaxed 1.625em line box, so the 1em chip shouldn't grow the row) — visual row-height check deferred to orchestrator QA. **(2) Unfeatured ⏭ meeting groups render as MeetingCards**: `EscalationsBlock` gains `asMeetingCards?: boolean` (BriefingContent passes `isNextSteps`); inside ⏭ Next steps each unfeatured meeting-ask group renders in the new `MeetingGroupCard` — the SAME `MeetingCard` shell as editor-featured entries: header is a dated meeting pill wrapped in `<strong>` (the heading-grade form; no editor lead exists, and the summary-pill means no `meetingRel` header pill — it would duplicate) + the shell's "N pending" count (pending = items without a verdict); expansion contents are UNCHANGED — the same decidable `LoopItemRow` ask rows (smallest correct change: shell swap only). The pill's rel path: `meetingKey()` (which already parsed the group key from `citations[0].source`) now also returns `rel` — the full `meetings/YYYY-MM-DD/….md` match (`match[0]`, prefix-agnostic). Non-⏭ sections and the fallback fold keep `MeetingGroupRow` (the bold-title + "N asks · ISO date" row); old briefings unaffected — the block only renders live escalations. Suites: briefing 40, vitest 70 green; tsc clean.

- **Agent-home hardening (adversarial round)** — Two findings fixed: (1) `parseLifecycle` now strips 🆕 from DONE titles — a task checked off before ever being viewed kept the literal emoji on done rows and cards forever (the read-receipt only fires for state "new"); (2) the 🆕 marker is stamped only once the mirror is past every gate (v2 list exists, not already linked), so a v1/absent week can no longer strand an unstrippable marker in the task file; the repeat-verdict self-heal path explicitly never re-marks (mark is opt-in per call path).

- **Dated meeting pills: the instance date lives INSIDE the chip, never bolted on after it** — Justin's B5 pill-date feedback ("not good… should feel like natural UI versus text bolted on"): the briefing's ⏭ headlines rendered a meeting pill followed by a literal bold "(7/7)". **(1) `ObjectPill` gains an integrated date segment** for `kind=meeting`: after the label, a muted "· Jul 7" (house three-letter-month form via `formatHiltMonthDay`; year appended only when not the current year — "· Dec 12, 2025"), derived at render with zero fetch from the ref id's `meetings/YYYY-MM-DD/…` path via the new pure `meetingDateSegment(rel, now?)` in `src/lib/briefing/canvas.ts` (timezone-safe: Date built from Y/M/D parts at noon, never `Date.parse` of a bare date string). New prop `showDate?: boolean` — default TRUE (an instance reference is the norm; the DATED variant), FALSE = the DATELESS series-level variant; ignored for other kinds. Styling: `.hilt-object-pill-date` — `var(--text-tertiary)`, normal weight, same baseline, `flex-shrink: 0` so the label ellipsizes first. Every existing caller gets the dated variant for free (briefing inline pills, `EscalationsPanel` citations, `TaskCard` meeting attribution). **(2) Redundant date-token suppression (renderer, defensive)**: new pure `stripDateAfterMeetingPill(markdown)` in `canvas.ts`, applied in `BriefingContent` alongside `normalizeHiltLinks` so it covers every render site — strips a literal date token (" (7/7)", " (2026-07-07)", " (Jul 7)"/" (Jul 7, 2026)", optionally bold-wrapped) ONLY when it directly follows a `hilt:meeting` link's closing `)` or its closing `**` wrapper, same line; dates elsewhere, dates after non-meeting links, and non-date parentheticals are untouched (covers today's already-written briefing + future model slips). **(3) Callers choosing dateless**: `MeetingCard`'s structural header pill passes `showDate={false}` — it renders only when the editor did NOT inline a pill, i.e. the lead uses the old "meeting (date)" house form and already carries the date in prose (every pre-B5 briefing), so a dated pill would double it; the ISO tooltip stays. `EscalationsPanel`'s `meetingCitationLabel` drops its "· 2026-07-05" ISO suffix — the dated pill's own segment replaces it in house form. **(4) Generator contract** (one sentence each): prompt `PILL CITATIONS` + the vault SKILL pill guidance now say the meeting pill CARRIES its instance date — never write a date token after a meeting pill; the "meeting (date)" house form applies only when no pill is used. Suites: briefing 40, objects 28, vitest 70 green; tsc clean.

- **Agent tasks get a home: "Ready for agents" weekly section + 🆕 on every verdict-promoted task** — Justin's approved decision: accepted-agent tasks must not be invisible, and every promotion should be amber-flagged until seen. **(1) `assign_to_agent` now mirrors into the weekly list too** — `POST /api/loops/verdicts` splices the accepted-agent task's v2 line into a `### Ready for agents` section of the current weekly list ("scoped and ready for an agent to process, just not run yet"), via the new section-aware splice `insertWeeklyV2LineInSection(content, line, heading)` in `src/lib/bridge/weekly-v2-view.ts`: case-insensitive heading match inside the Tasks region, splice at the section's top (skipping blanks, the `insertWeeklyV2Line` convention); a missing section is CREATED at the bottom of the Tasks region (before the next `## ` heading or EOF); content with no `## Tasks` degrades to appending the section at the end of the body — degrade, never corrupt, so it never returns null. - **Dismissal visibility is consistent everywhere + owner metadata renders as chips** — Three follow-ups from Justin's v3 feedback round, one theme: a dismissal is out of sight but never invisible, and owner brackets are data, not reading material. **(1) The briefing's ⏭ MeetingCard gains the dismissed tail**: `NextStepsMeetingItem` (B3) now renders the same quiet "Dismissed · N" divider tail as the meeting view (B2) and the Priorities Proposals section (A6) — classes copied exactly — scoped to that card's meeting and rendered only when N > 0. **(2) Limbo dismissals move to the tail immediately, everywhere**: the sighted bug — a dismissed ask whose proposal file is already deleted but whose LEDGER stamp waits for the loop's next run lingered as a "Dismiss"-badged card in the unminted-ask lanes. Note the deliberate lag: a dismiss deletes the proposal file instantly, but the LEDGER stamp lands at the loop's next run — the tail shows the ledger's record, not an optimistic echo. **(3) Verdict button clarity**: every TaskCard verdict button carries a plain-language `title` tooltip of its effect (Approve = "Take this on — becomes your task and joins this week's list"; Assign to agent = "Mark as agent work (agent execution arrives in Phase C)"; Dismiss = "Decline — removed; the loop remembers and won't re-propose it"; Revise = "Send a correction — returns for a fresh verdict"). - **B3 hardening (adversarial round)** — Two findings fixed before the first canvas morning: (1) the bullet-binding join now matches EITHER id form (`ma-` ledger id or minted `t-` task id) — binding only on `ma-` classified every ⏭-featured proposal as unfeatured, re-rendering the whole meeting group below the MeetingCard that already carried its TaskCards (the exact rollup anti-pattern rejected 2026-07-03); (2) an id-only line whose task file vanished out-of-band now keeps its raw token as an inert chip instead of stripping to empty and disappearing (never-drop). - **B2 hardening (adversarial round)** — Two findings fixed: (1) the shared event socket now REFCOUNTS channel subscriptions — B2's task hook inside MeetingEntry was the first child-component subscriber to a channel its parent view also uses, and its unmount unsubscribed the whole "bridge" channel, silently stopping the People sidebar's live updates until refocus (a latent flaw in the non-refcounted API that every future child subscriber would have tripped); (2) `useEscalations` no longer discards last-good data on a transient poll failure — one failed /api/loops/escalations request made ask-only Next-steps sections vanish for a full 60s refresh interval and reappear.

- **v3 Phase 2 (unit B2): meeting "Next steps" section — each meeting shows its own task proposals and landed tasks** — `MeetingEntry`'s Notes tab gains a fourth accordion section, "Next steps" (`ListTodo` icon, collapsed by default with a count in the header — the house `NotesAccordionSection` idiom, which now supports an optional `count`), rendered ONLY when the meeting produced something (no empty shell). Three lanes, one meeting, joined by the vault-relative meeting path (pure logic in the new `src/lib/tasks/meeting-next-steps.ts`): **(1) proposals** — task files in `tasks/.proposals/` whose `origin.meeting` equals this meeting's path, rendered as the shared A6 `TaskCard` with verdict controls POSTing the exact ProposalsSection body (`{ loop, item_id, verdict, note? }` → `/api/loops/verdicts`, then mutate both data sources; the origin-less-proposal read-only guard carries over); **(2) escalated-but-unminted ledger asks** (pre-Phase-A history) — items from `useEscalations` (reused from `EscalationsPanel`, no briefing props dragged along) of ask kind whose citation cites this meeting and whose `loop`+`item_id` has NO minted task file in either store (dedupe against both `proposals` and `tasks` `origin.item_id`), shaped as TaskFiles (`askToTaskFile`) so the same card renders them — undecided asks are decidable (the route absorbs the verdict; `file_effect: missing` is normal), decided ones show their verdict badge via TaskCard's new `verdict` seed prop; **(3) accepted/in-progress/done tasks** born from this meeting — read-only cards with a subtle status badge (TaskCard's new `showStatus` prop; `dropped` stays hidden — resurrecting a dismissal would undo A7). All cards pass `hideMeeting` (new prop) since the meeting attribution line is redundant inside its own meeting. The meeting's path derives from `meeting.filePath` by stripping the `vaultPath` prefix (fallback: last `meetings/` segment), matching the loop's `opened_from` stamp exactly. Live updates: `useTasksList` already revalidates on the `tasks-changed` WS event; the meeting data itself keeps flowing through the existing people pipeline. Join/dedupe/path logic is node:test covered in `meeting-next-steps.test.ts` (11 cases, wired into `test:tasks`); no component tests (no `.test.tsx` precedent — browser QA covers it).

- **B1 hardening (adversarial round)** — Two findings fixed: (1) the run timeout killed only the `npx` wrapper — the real tsx worker survived as an orphan holding the stdio pipes open, wedging the serial queue until a ws-server restart; the spawn is now `detached` with a process-GROUP kill on timeout and resolves on `exit` (live-verified: a hung 300s run timed out at exactly 60s, the queued meeting ran immediately after, zero orphans); (2) note-only meetings (audio off — transcript never appears) could never fire; stable transcript ABSENCE now settles on a doubled quiet window, so enhanced-notes-only meetings extract within ~5 minutes instead of waiting for the nightly.

- **v3 Phase 2 (unit B1): post-meeting extraction trigger — the meeting-actions loop runs minutes after a meeting ends** — New `src/lib/granola/extraction-trigger.ts`, hosted by the granola sync daemon inside ws-server. Each incremental sync cycle now reports its meeting docs (`setGranolaPostSyncObserver` in `sync.ts`; the observer is registered ONLY by `daemon.ts`, so manual syncs from other processes never fire — single writer for the trigger state). **Settle rule (enhanced-notes-first, quality over speed per the settled Phase-2 decision)**: a meeting fires when its vault note has enhanced-notes content (Granola's post-meeting AI panel — the strongest "meeting is over" signal) AND its transcript has stopped growing for **3 consecutive sync polls spanning ≥ 2 minutes** (the wall-clock floor guards against the 5s fast poll declaring a mid-meeting lull settled; both knobs env-tunable: `HILT_MEETING_TRIGGER_SETTLE_POLLS` / `HILT_MEETING_TRIGGER_SETTLE_MS`). Only meetings ≤2 days old are candidates (older unprocessed ones are the nightly's job). **Once-guard**: per-granola_id `fired_at` persisted to `$DATA_DIR/loops/meeting-trigger-state.json` (atomic writes, 14-day prune, survives ws-server restarts; stamped BEFORE spawning so a crashed run can't re-fire — the nightly is the net), plus a consult of the loop's own `processed-meetings.json` (home resolved exactly like the loop script: registry phase shadow → `$DATA_DIR/loops-shadow/meta/loops/meetings/state/`) so a meeting the nightly already read never fires; registry unreadable → fire nothing that cycle. **Serialized runner**: `SerialMeetingRunner` runs ONE `npx tsx scripts/loop-meeting-actions.ts --meetings-file <tmp json>` child at a time (ledger single-writer; a meeting settling mid-run queues, deduped, behind it), env passed through, deliberately NO `--proposals-dir`/`--ledger-home` flags so registry precedence resolves sinks exactly like the 19:30 nightly (which stays untouched as the safety net; the eval harness' `--ledger-home` isolation is untouched too). Exit code + output tail land in the daemon log (`[MeetingTrigger]` prefix); a run failure or timeout (15 min default) never kills the daemon. **Gate**: `HILT_MEETING_TRIGGER` — default ON whenever the granola daemon is enabled, `=0` disables instantly. Settle detection, once-guard, recency parsing, state pruning/persistence, and queue serialization (two enqueues → strictly sequential; failing run never wedges) are pure-function/node:test covered in `extraction-trigger.test.ts` (`test:granola`). Activation requires a ws-server bounce (the daemon lives there).

- **A7 hardening round 2 (the sweep's reviewer swept the sweep)** — Two gaps in readers the sweep missed, both fixed: (1) a malformed meeting note (broken frontmatter) crashed the whole loop run AND wedged every later run behind the unprocessed file — now degrades to a per-meeting warn+skip (verified live: hostile note → warn, run exits 0, artifact written); (2) a CORRUPT ledger.json was silently swallowed into an empty ledger that the run then persisted — one torn write wiped every dismiss verdict, task_id stamp, and first_escalated_at, destroying dismissed-immunity itself; readLedger now fails LOUD on corrupt (missing still starts empty) — a crash is recoverable, a persisted wipe is not.

- **v3 Phase 1 (unit A7): hardening — dismissed-immunity + missing-file degradation sweep** — Closes Phase A. **Dismissed-immunity**: the meeting extractor previously saw only the OPEN ledger for identity resolution, so a meeting restating a previously-DISMISSED commitment minted a brand-new ledger entry — and a brand-new proposal for work Justin already declined. Dismissal is now durable, three layers deep: (1) `recentlyDismissedEntries`/`dismissedLedgerDigest` (`src/lib/loops/meeting-ledger.ts`) collect entries dropped via a dismiss VERDICT within the last 30 days (`DISMISSED_IMMUNITY_DAYS`, matching the meeting backfill window — closure drops carry no verdict and are deliberately excluded) by reading the drop transition's `status_history` timestamp, and `buildExtractorTask` rides them into every extraction as a `=== RECENTLY DISMISSED ===` section (`id · owner · action`, omitted when empty); (2) the extractor prompt (v2.1, behavioral rule not extraction tuning — gold-set behavior unchanged) gains the rule that a commitment matching a recently-dismissed entry is a SIGHTING of that id, NEVER a new entry, with genuinely-new scope still minting; (3) belt-and-suspenders at ledger-apply time (`scripts/loop-meeting-actions.ts`): a NEW commitment whose normalized action text exactly matches a recently-dismissed entry (`recentlyDismissedByAction`/`normalizeActionText`) folds into that entry as a sighting instead of minting. Verified (and now documented in-code + spec-tested): sightings record evidence ONLY — applying one to a dropped entry never changes status, and dropped entries can never re-escalate (escalation/aging iterate `openEntries`), re-mint (`task_id` stamp + verdict persist), or re-close. New `src/lib/loops/meeting-ledger.test.ts` (window/verdict filtering incl. the closure-drop exclusion, digest format, prompt section presence/order/omission, prompt-rule presence, normalized exact-match index). **Degradation sweep** (every reader joining task/ledger/proposal data, missing/corrupt inputs must degrade + warn, never crash): verified already-degrading — `/api/tasks` GET (corrupt file → `readTaskDir` skip+warn), `/api/bridge/weekly` GET (missing task file → raw line + `missing: true`, A3), ProposalsSection (origin-less proposal renders read-only), verdict route (corrupt proposal → `listProposals` skips → `file_effect: "missing"`, any file-effect throw degrades with the verdict already recorded), loop verdict-apply (ledger-only, unknown ids skipped; task files never read), escalations route (never dereferences `task_id`; per-loop errors collected, malformed verdict stores caught per loop). ONE gap found and fixed: `readTask`/`readProposal` threw on a CORRUPT (vs missing) file, so `GET /api/tasks/[id]` answered 500 for a bricked file — both now degrade to null with a warn (the id route answers 404), matching the store's own documented "reads degrade to missing, mutations throw" contract; mutations on a bricked file now throw the honest `task not found` (tested in `tasks.test.ts`).

### Changed

- **Library series parents can use source-appropriate formats** — Data-model docs now describe series parents as generic Library reference artifacts (`series_role: parent`) with a source-appropriate `format` such as `video-series` or `newsletter`, rather than implying every parent is a YouTube/video-series object. This matches the Pragmatic Engineer newsletter series now using the same parent/child Library series feature.

- **v3 Phase 0 cutover complete: the loops-fed briefing IS the briefing** — `briefing:daily` (the 6:00 launchd job) now carries `--loops`, so THE vault briefing reads every enabled loop's latest artifact; the 6:20 `com.hilt.loops.shadow-v2` job and its `briefing:shadow:v2` npm script are retired (plist booted + deleted), and the retry watcher covers the single briefing. The `$VAULT/meta/briefing-shadow` symlink is removed; the shadow-period briefings remain read-only history in `$DATA/briefing-shadow/`. The memo's `/api/reports/memo` HTML render now uses a plain-markdown scratch copy (same frontmatter fix the morning report got). Verified end-to-end: manual `briefing:daily` produced a valid 4KB loops-fed briefing (14 loop citations), committed + pushed; browser QA confirmed the single pane, escalation nesting, all four verdict controls, and both verdict/feedback POSTs round-tripping. HOW-IT-WORKS updated to the one-symlink storage truth and single-briefing rhythm.

- **Library morning report + editor's memo re-pointed to the loop home (single-write)** — The 05:10 steering run no longer writes the legacy `meta/library-reports/YYYY-MM-DD.md` copy; the loop artifact at `meta/loops/references/reports/YYYY-MM-DD.md` is now the ONE vault write (the `/api/reports/morning` HTML remote surface is rendered from a scratch markdown copy, since the loop artifact carries YAML frontmatter `report-html.ts` would render literally). The Sunday editor's memo now writes to `meta/loops/references/memos/YYYY-MM-DD-editors-memo.md` instead of `references/process/memos/` (same filename and frontmatter format). The briefing link resolver (`src/lib/bridge/briefing-link-targets.ts`, behind `/api/bridge/briefings/link-target`) reads the loop homes first and falls back to the legacy dirs for dates that only exist there, so old briefing links keep resolving; loop-home memos open in Docs (they live outside the library scanner's `references/` root), legacy memos still open as library items.

### Added

- **A6 hardening (adversarial round)** — Four findings fixed: (1) free-text extractor dues ("next sprint", ~15% of ledger dues) no longer reach the `due` field — ISO dues stamp frontmatter, stated text lands in the body ("Due (as stated): …"), and `DueBadge` guards Invalid Date anyway (an unguarded `Intl.format` throw would have crashed the whole Priorities render); (2) the `task_id` stamp persists to the ledger immediately after EACH mint (the crash window between mint and the end-of-pass save re-minted the whole set as duplicates); (3) contradictory verdicts: a dismiss after an earlier approve now DROPS the accepted task (`via verdict:dismiss`) instead of reporting "already-applied" while the ledger diverged; (4) revise no longer locks a TaskCard's verdict controls for the session — the card stays decidable, matching the briefing's revise-re-escalates idiom.

- **v3 Phase 1 (unit A6): proposal minting + synchronous verdict file-apply + Proposals section** — Meeting-loop asks become task PROPOSAL FILES at escalation time; verdicts apply the file effect synchronously; Priorities gains a Proposals section. **Minting** (`src/lib/loops/proposal-mint.ts`): `mintProposalFromLedgerEntry` maps a LedgerEntry → proposal file (action → title; first citation's anchor+source → `provenance { quote, source }`; meeting path + ledger id + loop id → `origin`; `due` carries) and stamps `entry.task_id` — the idempotency guard: a stamped entry NEVER re-mints, surviving loop re-runs and deliberate file deletion (a dismissed proposal can't resurrect). The stamp rides the loop's existing ledger persistence. `resolveProposalSink` is the ONE precedence rule (pure, unit-tested): `--proposals-dir` → explicit; `--ledger-home` → `<home>/proposals/` (the eval harness `launchpad-extractor-eval.ts` is isolated with ZERO changes — verified it invokes the loop only via `--ledger-home`); registry `proposal_sink: "vault"` → `<vault>/tasks/.proposals/`; else `<loopHome>/proposals/` (shadow default). `scripts/loop-meeting-actions.ts` mints inside the escalation pass (volume gates carry over free — only entries that escalate ever mint), gains `--proposals-dir`/`--no-proposals`, tolerates per-entry mint failures (ask still escalates; health notes count them), and reports `proposal_sink`/`proposals_minted` in its run JSON. The registry key is SUPPORTED end-to-end (`RegistryLoop.proposal_sink`, validated to `"vault"` in `parseRegistry`) but deliberately NOT flipped in the real registry — the loop stays shadow-sinked until the A-gate. **Store primitive** (`createProposalIn` in `src/lib/tasks/store.ts`, closing the A2 review gap): mints a `proposed` task file into an ARBITRARY sink dir with the same exclusive-create (`wx` + re-mint on EEXIST) discipline, id collision-checked against the sink AND — via `collisionBaseDir` — the vault's canonical `tasks/` + `.proposals/` (`mintTaskIdAcross` in `ids.ts`), so ids minted outside the vault never collide inside it. **Verdict route** (`POST /api/loops/verdicts`): after the UNCHANGED jsonl append (audit trail + the loop's ledger-effect queue), the route now applies the proposal FILE effect synchronously — approve visibly produces the task NOW. Join: the proposal's `origin.item_id` + `origin.loop` (the ledger id IS the verdict item id; no client change). approve/assign_to_me → `approveProposal` accepted-me; assign_to_agent → accepted-agent; dismiss → `dismissProposal` (file deleted; the ledger remembers); revise → note appended, stays proposed. Response gains `file_effect: "applied" | "already-applied" | "missing"` (missing = no vault proposal file — normal for pre-A6 items and non-vault sinks); repeat verdicts are idempotent (the accepted-task probe answers already-applied); a file-effect crash never loses the recorded verdict (record-first order, degrade + log). Single-writer map holds: the route owns the proposal FILE lifecycle, the loop owns the LEDGER (its verdict-apply pass is untouched and never re-mints a stamped entry) — the two can't fight. **UI**: new pure-props `src/components/tasks/TaskCard.tsx` (title, due badge, muted truncated provenance quote, origin meeting; hover-revealed Approve / Assign to agent / Dismiss / Revise-with-note controls in the EscalationsPanel idiom, POSTing left to the surface) rendered by the ONE new surface `src/components/tasks/ProposalsSection.tsx` in the Priorities view (`BridgeView`): `useTasksList()` proposals, renders ONLY when proposals exist (no empty shell), collapsed-by-default count header matching the Done accordion, verdicts POST the same body the briefing uses then mutate — file + ledger effects both flow, and the file write also comes back via `tasks-changed`. Briefing ask UI untouched (it gets the file semantics for free through the same endpoint); full card unification is deliberately deferred to Phase B. Tests: `src/lib/loops/proposal-mint.test.ts` (mapping fidelity, task_id idempotency incl. deleted-file case, sink precedence, cross-dir collision, registry key validation) + `src/app/api/loops/verdicts/route.test.ts` (each verdict kind's file effect, repeat = already-applied, no-file = missing/absorbed, same-loop join, validation regressions; wired into `test:vitest`). No TaskCard component tests (no `.test.tsx` precedent).

- **A5 hardening (adversarial round)** — Two rerun findings fixed: (1) recycling into an existing week now answers 409 (a sequential rerun treated the NEW list as current — the v1/v2 checkbox-regex asymmetry then minted garbage task files and dropped lines); (2) a retry after a failed new-list write reuses the prior attempt's minted task files (matched by `origin.list` + title + `accepted-me`) instead of double-minting the whole carried set.

- **v3 Phase 1 (unit A5): the weekly recycle mints the NEXT week as a v2 (task-file-backed) list** — `POST /api/bridge/recycle` now builds the v2 skeleton ITSELF: after interpolating the template it injects `list_format: 2` into the new file's frontmatter immediately after the `week:` line (`injectListFormat2` in the new `src/lib/bridge/recycle-v2.ts`) — template anchors are never trusted (the template body is preamble/Notes only; a missing `## Tasks` anchor gets the section appended). Carried-task conversion (`buildV2CarrySection`) WALKS the outgoing file's task-section lines rather than trusting only the parse: **(1) v1 task line** → `createTask` (title; `[due:: …]` → frontmatter `due`; title project links → frontmatter `projects`; indent-stripped details → body with the trailing blank run trimmed; born `accepted-me`; `origin: { list: "lists/now/<outgoing>.md" }` — new optional `TaskOrigin.list` key) + a `renderWeeklyV2Line` line in the new list; **(2) v2 task line** (a later v2→v2 recycle) → the EXISTING task file is relinked, never re-minted (one identity for a unit of work), with hand-added list sub-bullets riding along verbatim; **(3) unresolvable content** — a task whose conversion fails (e.g. whitespace-only title), a v2 line whose file is missing, and stray non-task lines the v1 parser silently dropped (including strays interleaved INSIDE a task block, which rawLines skip over) — carries VERBATIM, never skipped, rendering via the v2 missing/linkless degradation path. `###` group structure is preserved exactly the way the v1 recycle preserved it (heading emitted on a carried task's group change). Done tasks keep the existing behavior: the modal never offers them, and nothing is minted for them. The OUTGOING file stays byte-untouched except the pre-existing accomplishments write (byte-verified in tests against `updateAccomplishments`' exact output). **Data preservation** (plan rule, since the first v2 recycle converts the daily driver): before any write the route snapshots `lists/now/*.md` to `$DATA_DIR/backups/<date>-recycle-v2/` — best-effort with logging, never overwriting an existing snapshot (the first copy of the day, the pre-recycle state, wins). Response is additive: `{ filename, listFormat: 2, tasksCreated, tasksRelinked, verbatimLines }`. Route-level vitest spec (`src/app/api/bridge/recycle/route.test.ts`, wired into `test:bridge`) recycles a byte-exact checked-in copy of the REAL live week (`src/lib/bridge/__fixtures__/recycle-v2/2026-07-13.md`) asserting line-by-line file fidelity (title/due/projects/body/origin/status per carried task), plus a hostile fixture (unicode, mid-title `[due::]`, tab nesting, stray prose between tasks, whitespace-only title → verbatim), a v2→v2 relink case, the snapshot, and the anchor-less template path.

- **v3 Phase 1 (unit A4): Priorities dual render — v2 lists in the UI, v1 pixel-identical** — The Priorities view now renders task-file-backed (`list_format: 2`) weekly lists with the same look and interactions as v1; every branch keys on the presence of a store-resolvable `taskPath` (v1 tasks never carry one), so v1 lists are untouched. **Task panel** (`BridgeTaskPanel`): for a v2 task the DETAILS editor's data source is the task FILE body via `useTaskFile(taskIdFromTaskPath(taskPath))`, saved with `PUT /api/tasks/[id] { body }` (the A2 route); title/due/checkbox edits keep flowing through `PUT /api/bridge/tasks/[id]` — the A3 write-through router. `keepPreviousData` is guarded (`fileTask.id === v2TaskId`) so a just-switched selection never feeds another task's body into the editor, and the editor's `filePath` points at the task file so image drops land relative to it. A `missing: true` line (task file absent/unreadable, or a linkless plain line) renders a quiet degraded panel: raw title (read-only), the muted one-liner "Task file missing — this line renders from the weekly list only.", no editor; Attach-project/Due-date menu items hidden (they'd need the file), copy + delete kept. **Rows** (`BridgeTaskItem`): `missing` lines get a small muted `Unlink` marker (tooltip "Task file missing"); otherwise v1 and v2 rows are visually identical — positional selection, drag/reorder, groups, and moveTo keep operating on the list-as-view (rawLines round-trip verbatim per A3). **ProjectPicker persistence**: v2 tasks write task frontmatter `projects` via `PUT /api/tasks/[id] { projects: [...] }` (`null` clears); v1 keeps the legacy `projectPaths` write-through (shared `persistTaskProjects` branch in `useBridgeWeekly`). **v2 add, end to end**: `POST /api/bridge/tasks` replaces the A3 stopgap 409 with a real branch — `createTask(vault, { title, status: "accepted-me" })` FILE FIRST, then the rendered line (`renderWeeklyV2Line`) is spliced surgically into the top of the task section by the new `insertWeeklyV2Line` (directly under `## Tasks`, before any `###` group — v1's insertion convention; heading-less lists insert before the first task/group line; NEVER the v1 serializer). A failed splice/list-write is the A3 mirror-failure contract: warn + 200 + `mirrorFailed: true` (the task file, the truth, exists; A6's surfaces will show it). Response shape matches v1's `{ task }` (hydrated, `task-0`). POST also now rejects whitespace-only titles with 400 (an empty v2 title would collapse the link markup). **Plumbing**: `isValidTaskId` moved to pure `src/lib/tasks/task-id.ts` and `taskIdFromTaskPath` to the pure `src/lib/tasks/weekly-v2.ts` (hand-rolled posix-style normalization, no `node:path`) so client components can branch on v2-ness — both re-exported from their old homes (`store.ts`, `weekly-v2-view.ts`) so no server consumer changed. Optimistic toggles are unchanged (v2 flows through the same `PUT /api/bridge/tasks/[id]` + SWR mutate; the extra `tasks-changed` event dedupes via SWR). Tests: 4 new POST cases in the A3 route vitest (v2 add file+line placement, mirror-write failure, no-anchor fallback, v1 legacy path) + 4 `insertWeeklyV2Line` unit cases in `weekly-v2.test.ts` (one-line-diff splice, blank-line skip, heading-less fallback, null anchor). No component tests (no `.test.tsx` precedent — browser QA covers it).

- **A3 hardening (adversarial round)** — Four confirmed findings fixed the same night: (1) v2 PUT validates title/details/projectPaths BEFORE any write and `updateTask` itself rejects empty titles — a cleared title wrote an unparseable task file, permanently bricking the task (HIGH); (2) DELETE gained its v2 branch: file-first (active tasks transition to `dropped` with a `via weekly-delete` History line; done tasks keep their status — the work happened), then the line (plus consecutive hand-added sub-bullets) is removed surgically via `removeWeeklyLines`, never through the v1 serializer; (3) POST add on a v2 list answers a deliberate 409 instead of a generic 500 (v2 add lands in A4); (4) a hand-quoted `list_format: "2"` marker now keys v2 (the bridge frontmatter parser keeps YAML quote chars) — previously every checkbox click on such a list silently diverged from the task files.

- **v3 Phase 1 (unit A3): weekly list v2 read + write-through** — The weekly Priorities list can now be a *view over task files* (`list_format: 2` frontmatter) while v1 lists stay **byte-for-byte** on the legacy path. Parser (`src/lib/bridge/weekly-parser.ts`): surfaces `listFormat` (default 1) on `BridgeWeekly`; on v2 lists, task-line parsing delegates to the A1 primitive (`parseWeeklyV2Line`) — per-task `taskPath` = the LAST markdown-link target on the line, and `projectPaths` stays EMPTY (the v1 title-link project overload is dead in v2; projects live in task frontmatter). The v1 serializers (`updateTask`/`addTask`) now *throw* on v2 content — a corruption guard, since they would sever a line from its task file (v2 add/edit flows are owned by the routes; A4 wires the UI). New `src/lib/bridge/weekly-v2-view.ts`: `hydrateWeeklyTasks` (per-line join with task files — `title`/`done`/`due`/`projects` from the FILE; missing/unreadable/linkless line → the raw line's own data + `missing: true`, never dropped), `taskIdFromTaskPath` (only canonical `tasks/<t-…>.md` paths resolve; traversal and `.proposals/` rejected), and `replaceWeeklyLine` (surgical single-line replacement with startLine verification + unique-line fallback; `null` = cosmetic mirror failure, never corruption). `GET /api/bridge/weekly` hydrates v2 lists; response shape stays backward compatible (additive fields only: `listFormat`, `taskPath`, `missing`). `PUT /api/bridge/tasks/[id]` gains v2 branches keyed STRICTLY on the owning list's `listFormat === 2`: **task file written first (truth), list line mirrored second** — checkbox checked → audited `done` transition (`accepted-*` → done shortcut), unchecked → `in-progress` reopen, both `via weekly-checkbox` in the file's History; title/due → store patch then line re-render via `renderWeeklyV2Line`; details/projects → task file ONLY (weekly byte-untouched); mirror failure = warn + success + `mirrorFailed: true` (self-heals on the next hydrated read), file failure = 404/409 with the list untouched, NEVER list-first. Testing: **golden byte locks** — three REAL historical weekly lists copied into `src/lib/bridge/__fixtures__/weekly-v1/` (2026-01-27 legacy small; 2026-03-02 no-`## Tasks`-wrapper + 8 groups; 2026-03-16 large with due dates/groups/accomplishments) with a sha-256 manifest of every mutator's output generated against the pre-A3 parser (`weekly-goldens.test.ts`; regenerate only for a deliberate v1 change via `UPDATE_WEEKLY_GOLDENS=1`); a hand-authored v2 fixture vault (`__fixtures__/weekly-v2/`, including an intentionally missing task file); `weekly-v2.test.ts` (parser/hydration/helpers) and route-level vitest `src/app/api/bridge/tasks/[id]/route.test.ts` (write-through order, mirror-failure, degradation, v1 legacy path) — all wired into `test:bridge`. Notable discovery locked rather than fixed (v1 byte fidelity is the mandate): the v1 serializer's whitespace normalization is *cumulative* — every full rewrite adds one blank line per group boundary, which is why old weeklies carry huge blank runs. Recycle minting the first v2 list is unit A5.

- **v3 Phase 1 (unit A1): task-object core library** — New `src/lib/tasks/` implements the task primitive from the blessed v3 scope: one markdown file per task (`<vault>/tasks/<id>.md`), proposals as task files from birth in `tasks/.proposals/` (approve = status transition + rename into `tasks/`; dismiss = unlink, the meeting loop's ledger remembers; revise = note appended, stays proposed). Modules: `types.ts` (TaskFile + statuses `proposed | accepted-me | accepted-agent | in-progress | done | dropped`), `task-file.ts` (gray-matter parse/serialize with round-trip **byte fidelity** — unknown frontmatter keys survive in `extra`, bodies are never reformatted), `ids.ts` (`t-YYYYMMDD-NNN` minting, collision-checked across both dirs), `status.ts` (transition machine; every transition appends `- <ISO> status: a → b (via …)` under `## History`; `done → in-progress` is the checkbox-uncheck reopen), `store.ts` (baseDir-parameterized CRUD over `atomicWriteFile`, shared by loop scripts and API routes), `proposals.ts`, `weekly-v2.ts` (pure line helpers for `list_format: 2` weekly lists — parse/render `- [ ] [Title](tasks/t-….md) [due:: …]` lines, checkbox mirroring; the v1 weekly parser is untouched), and `hydrate.ts` (per-line degradation: missing/corrupt task file → raw line + `missing: true`, never throws, never drops). 22-test suite in `tasks.test.ts`; `npm run test:tasks` added and wired into `test:unit` after `test:loops`. Consumers land in A2–A6 (routes, weekly v2 read/write-through, proposal minting).

- **v3 Phase 1 (unit A2): task-object plumbing — watcher, events, API routes, hooks** — The A1 library is now wired end-to-end. **BridgeWatcher** watches `<vault>/tasks/` (ensuring `tasks/.proposals/` exists at start so a fresh vault has something to watch) and emits a debounced `tasks-changed` (`bridge` channel, `{}` payload) for changes in either store; the old blanket dot-ignore regex `/(^|[/\\])\../` — which would have hidden `.proposals/` — is replaced by `server/watchers/watch-ignore.ts` (`isIgnoredBridgePath`): dot-paths and `node_modules` stay ignored EXCEPT the `.proposals` directory directly under `tasks/` (dotfiles *inside* it, e.g. `.DS_Store`, are still ignored). Unit-tested (`watch-ignore.test.ts`, run by `test:tasks`). Graph + semantic runners subscribe to `tasks-changed` alongside `weekly-changed`, and `tasks` joined `INCLUDED_DIRS` in `src/lib/graph/build.ts` so the rescan actually covers task files (classified as plain `note` nodes; `.proposals/` excluded from the graph by the existing dotdir filter). New **`/api/tasks` routes** (deliberately NOT under `/api/bridge`): `GET /api/tasks` lists both stores; `GET /api/tasks/[id]` probes `tasks/` then `.proposals/` and reports `store`; `POST /api/tasks` creates (400 on validation, 201 on create); `PUT /api/tasks/[id]` patches non-status fields with JSON `null` → clear-the-key translation (the lib's undefined-clears convention; `title`/`body` not clearable), rejects `status` in a patch with a pointer to the `{ transition: { to, via } }` shape, which runs `transitionTask` — the shared audited path that appends the `## History` ledger line. Routes never broadcast — the file write → BridgeWatcher → EventServer is the only push path. New **`src/hooks/useTaskFile.ts`**: `useTaskFile(taskId)` and `useTasksList()` (SWR + `tasks-changed` revalidation, house `useBridgeWeekly` pattern) for the A4/A6 surfaces. Route behavior (null-clears, transition, status rejection, 404/409 split) is vitest-tested by direct handler invocation (`src/app/api/tasks/[id]/route.test.ts`, wired into `test:vitest`).
