- **Reference Library first-class series UI** — Series/course/playlist membership is now visible in the Library UI instead of hidden in frontmatter. Feed cards and list rows show compact series badges (`Part n of m` or `Series overview`), and the Library detail pane renders a native series panel under the title. Child items can open the parent overview/synthesis note and jump to sibling episodes without leaving the Library reader; parent notes show the overview plus the child map in the same surface. The panel uses the existing `/api/library?series=<id>` contract and Library item routes, so `references/series/*.md` parent notes remain markdown-backed but no longer require switching to Docs to inspect them.

- **Briefings v2 shadow-review comparison surface** — Added `GET /api/bridge/briefings/shadow?id=<briefingId>` to read the nightly `$DATA_DIR/briefing-shadow/` mirror without touching the vault, returning existence, stripped markdown content, and file mtime. The Briefing view now shows a session-only `Live | v2 shadow | Compare` segmented control when a selected briefing has a shadow file; shadow content reuses the live `BriefingContent` renderer, Compare stacks on narrow screens and splits into two columns with a subtle divider on wide screens, and the v2 pane posts whole-briefing feedback to the briefing loop. `/api/loops/feedback` now accepts the registry-present but disabled `briefing` loop for this shadow-period feedback path only.

- **Briefings v2 loop verdict/feedback capture surface** — Added `/api/loops/escalations` to gather escalated items from enabled live/shadow loop artifacts with per-loop error notes instead of hard failures, plus `/api/loops/verdicts` and `/api/loops/feedback` append-only writers for Justin-authored verdicts and free-form feedback. The Briefing view now renders a compact top-of-content "Awaiting your verdict" panel with escalated action/proposal verdict controls, feedback inputs for every item, existing-verdict badges, collapsed details, citations, and confidence metadata.

- **Reference Library series/playlist grouping** — Library items can now carry first-class `series` metadata (`series_id`, `series_title`, `series_url`, 1-based `series_index`, `series_total`, and `series_parent`) so a YouTube playlist/course can be ingested as individual child references without treating the playlist as duplicate content. The YouTube playlist adapter preserves playlist title/url/position metadata and maps configured playlist sources into series membership; saved references, candidates, promotion, search, and `/api/library?series=<id>` all round-trip the relationship. Added `npm run library:series:synthesize` to generate a dry-run-first parent series note (`references/series/<id>.md`) with a child map, plus optional `--analyze` to run the existing vault-aware reweave engine across the child notes for whole-series synthesis. Added the manual explicit-save source `youtube-stanford-cs153-frontier-systems` for the Stanford CS153 Frontier Systems playlist.

- **Library entries vs. sources — cross-source de-duplication with `cited_from` citations** — A library entry is the *content* (an article/video/episode); the sources are the places it was cited from. The same important content commonly arrives from more than one source with **different URLs** — most often a podcast episode that comes in via its YouTube channel feed AND the newsletter that announces it — which URL-dedup can't catch, so it landed as duplicate entries. New model: an entry keeps its primary `source_id` plus a `cited_from: Citation[]` list (the other sources), and connections are **unioned** across the merges so nothing is lost. New `src/lib/library/citations.ts` supplies the primitives: `contentMatchKeys` (YouTube video-id from the URL *or* an embedded `## Media` iframe; else a normalized title), `sourceRank` (primary content — a YouTube video/article — outranks a newsletter announcement), `findContentDuplicate`, and `appendCitationToFile` (folds a citation + unions `connection_suggestions` and the body `## Connections` section in place). Three integration points: (1) **ingest guard** in `processArtifact` — on a content match, fold the incoming source in as a citation instead of writing a duplicate; if the incoming source is *more* canonical (the video arriving after the newsletter mention), it becomes the entry and the thinner one is folded + removed; (2) **backfill** `scripts/library-dedupe.ts` (`npm run library:dedupe`, dry-run by default, `--write` to apply) merges existing cross-source pairs — YouTube canonical, union connections, remove the folded candidate (never deletes a *saved* reference); (3) **reader** shows "· also via Lenny's Podcast" on the source line. `cited_from` threads through promote/redigest (`ProcessedArtifact.cited_from`) so merged citations survive. Ran the backfill on the live vault: 4 podcast↔newsletter pairs merged (e.g. the Benedict Evans episode now carries 10 unioned connections + the newsletter citation). New `src/lib/library/citations.test.ts`.

- **Library video: per-video playback-speed control + speed no longer resets** — Library videos still default to **2×**, but the speed now *persists for the session*: changing it (via the new control or YouTube's own menu) sticks across pause/replay and across transcript-line seeks, instead of snapping back to 2× every time (`YouTubeEmbed.tsx`). Root cause was re-applying the *default* rate on every `onStateChange(PLAYING)` and every seek; it now tracks the user's current rate in a ref (seeded to the default, reset only when the video itself changes) and re-asserts *that*. A new `onPlaybackRateChange` subscription keeps the UI in sync with native menu changes. New **speed control** sits just below the player (per-video, so multi-video posts can each have their own): a `Gauge` pill showing the current rate that opens a popover of the player's available rates. YouTube's IFrame API only honors its own supported rates (0.25–2 in steps), so the control offers exactly what the player reports (no arbitrary >2× on YouTube). X/other non-YouTube embeds have no programmatic rate API, so this is YouTube-scoped.

- **Native Hilt briefing generator (Phase 0/1 — replacing the Hestia/Hermes cron)** — Justin's daily/weekend briefing is being migrated off the external Hermes agent (gpt‑5.5/openai‑codex on Hestia) to run natively in the Hilt stack on Mercury via Hilt's own `claude` CLI path — same vault skill + gatherer, no Hermes dependency. New `src/lib/briefing/`: `target-file.ts` (daily ISO path + weekend Saturday‑anchor logic, ported from `gather.sh`), `validator.ts` (the deterministic parity gate — canonical section spine + order, gold‑derived length band, fail‑closed "fresh editor's‑memo headline ⇒ `[Read the memo]` link required", mandatory `[Full library report]` link, no Sources section, footer; passes all four real gold briefings), `prompt.ts` (the vault `SKILL.md` verbatim + a harness "output discipline" block that enforces SKILL.md's concision intent Claude under‑honors vs gpt‑5.5), `generate.ts` (run gatherer → `claude -p` → validate → write → commit/push), and `vault-commit.ts` (per‑file commit+push — Hilt jobs don't commit today, which is what stranded briefings after the rename; this owns it). CLI `scripts/briefing-generate.ts` + `npm run briefing:generate` / `test:briefing`. Verified by two resumable multi‑agent **parity‑verification workflows** (deps‑green → native spike → adversarial judge panel) reaching **6/6 HIGH**, plus a real end‑to‑end production run producing a structurally‑valid, gold‑band (4.4 KB) daily briefing. The **shadow scheduler is now in place**: `src/lib/briefing/scheduler-jobs.ts` + `scripts/briefing-scheduler.ts` (shared `runScheduler`), with a single 06:00‑ET `--mode auto` job (daily Mon–Fri, weekend Sat/Sun) plus `scripts/briefing-retry.ts` (30‑min weekday watcher for the live variant). The **shadow** variant (`com.hilt.briefing.shadow`, installed on Mercury) writes to `$DATA_DIR/briefing-shadow/` and never commits — running alongside Hermes for a multi‑day parity comparison; first shadow run matched the same‑day Hermes gold on lead anchor, item selection, and voice. Remaining: the multi‑day shadow comparison, then cutover (`--variant live` + disabling Hermes's three briefing crons on Hestia).

- **Generalized authenticated browser recovery (`library:recover`)** — A source-agnostic sibling of `library-x-recover.ts` (`scripts/library-recover.ts`, `npm run library:recover`) recovers login-walled articles (LinkedIn pulse, and anything digestion flags `needs_auth_recovery`) when even the Raindrop cache is just a sign-in gate. It drives `browser-harness` (attaches to the signed-in Chrome on the recovery host), extracts the real article with a generic readable-content DOM extractor, replaces the Raw Content, runs a cache-preferring redigest (which now summarizes the recovered text), and stamps `reweave_pending` for the nightly weave. It shares `loginWallVerdict`/`LOGIN_WALL_PATTERNS` with capture-health so the two recovery surfaces detect the same walls. Manual-only (`--path` / `--bucket` / `--dry-run`), one-time `chrome://inspect` CDP authorize. New `ProcessedArtifact.needs_auth_recovery` frontmatter signal threads through `references.ts` + `library-redigest.ts` (cleared on successful recovery).

- **Unified "Copy reference" service** — A portable reference (location + one-line how-to + title) can now be copied for any Hilt object and pasted straight into a coding agent, which then knows what the object is, where it lives, and how to access it. Previously this lived in ~11 bespoke, duplicated copy handlers with no shared code. New centralized service `src/lib/references/`: `clipboard.ts` (one `copyToClipboard` with the legacy textarea fallback, replacing two copy-pasted impls), `types.ts` (`HiltRef` discriminated union — one variant per object kind), and `build.ts` (`buildReference` — the single place reference content is tuned; pure + unit-tested in `build.test.ts`, which byte-locks the original Bridge-task format). React layer: `useCopyReference()` hook (`src/hooks/`) and a drop-in `CopyReferenceButton` (`src/components/ui/`). File-backed references lead with an **absolute** path (a local agent can open it immediately); session leads with the externalId; calendar leads with a `GET /api/calendar/events/:id` fetch hint. The existing copy sites were migrated onto it (Bridge task, Library, Docs, Meetings, People, Stack plugin/MCP, Sessions), and it was added to two surfaces that lacked it: **Bridge briefing items** (hover-revealed icon per item; the reference points at the briefing file + headline so an agent can find the bullet and its source/trace) and **Calendar events** (icon in the event popover header). The trigger itself is now uniform too — every "Copy reference" affordance shows the same **clipboard (`Copy`) icon and "Copy reference" label/tooltip** (previously a mix of "Copy path", "Copy markdown path", "Copy session ID" with `Link2`/`Copy` icons); Bridge's separate "Copy as markdown" moved to a `FileText` icon to stay distinct. Adding a new surface is now a one-line `buildReference` case + a `CopyReferenceButton`. Supporting data-model additions: `LibraryArtifact.abs_path` and `BriefingDetail.absPath` (both populated where the absolute path is already known, so the client can build absolute references). New `npm run test:references`. Deferred (trivial to add later): Projects, Thoughts, Areas, Weekly lists, Granola meetings.

- **System Agent runtime (read-only observer mode)** — Implemented `docs/plans/system-agent-mode.md`: `server/system-agent.ts` is a lightweight Node HTTP runtime (NOT Next.js) that lets an observer machine such as Hestia appear in another machine's System views (Sync, Apps, Sessions, Stack) without running the full Hilt stack — no UI, `ws-server`, Bridge/Library write routes, Granola/calendar daemons, or graph/semantic runners. It binds `127.0.0.1:${HILT_SYSTEM_AGENT_PORT:-3200}` and is exposed to peers via Tailscale Serve (origin root → `127.0.0.1:3200`); it never listens on a tailnet interface. Handlers are thin wrappers over the same `@/lib` functions the full Hilt routes call, so agent output is byte-identical to full Hilt's local output (proven by `scripts/system-agent-parity.ts`). The route surface is a strict 12-route allowlist (machine, sync, sync/conflicts, local-apps[, /refresh, /previews/:file], stack[, /file], map work-graph/sessions/session-detail/refresh); every other path is a compact JSON 404 with no HTML, and there is no peer fan-out (the agent answers only local snapshots). Discovery needed **no change** to `src/lib/system/peers.ts` logic — the existing `fetchPeerSystemMachine` already accepts any responder with `app==="hilt-system" && enabled===true && machine`. The only contract change is an additive `role: "full" | "agent"` field on `SystemMachineResponse` (`src/lib/system/types.ts`): the full app emits `"full"`, the agent emits `"agent"` (with `app_server: null`, i.e. no mode-switch surface), and `fetchPeerSystemMachine` reads `data.role` onto the discovered `SystemMachine` so Mercury can badge an agent. Deployed as a single KeepAlive LaunchAgent `com.hilt.system-agent` via `scripts/system-agent-launchd.ts` + `scripts/hilt-system-agent.sh` (tailscale-aware PATH, no Granola/daemon env, dedicated `${DATA_DIR}/system-agent.json` heartbeat distinct from the supervisor's `app-supervisor.json`). New npm scripts: `system-agent:run|install|uninstall|status` and `test:system-agent[:e2e|:parity|:smoke|:all]`. Verified by a layered suite — in-process allowlist/404/no-HTML unit tests (`server/system-agent.test.ts`), a single-host e2e that boots the real agent and proves no daemon artifacts touch `DATA_DIR` (`scripts/system-agent-e2e.ts`), agent-vs-full byte parity (`scripts/system-agent-parity.ts`), and a wire smoke reusable against a remote Serve origin (`scripts/system-agent-smoke.ts`). New env var `HILT_SYSTEM_AGENT_PORT` (default `3200`) — add it to `.env.example`.

- **System Agent mode implementation plan** — Added `docs/plans/system-agent-mode.md`, the implementation plan (Context → milestones M0–M6 → verification matrix → definition of done) for the observer runtime above.

- **System ▸ Performance subtab (Mercury closet/compute telemetry)** — A new `performance` System subtab visualizes the standalone Mercury observability stream (closet temp/humidity/motion, ambient/outdoor temp, CPU/GPU die temps + power draw, memory, load) so closet temperature can be correlated with compute heat/load over time for airflow tuning. The Mercury collector + server stay on Mercury (port 8787); Hilt reads them through server-side proxy routes `GET /api/system/mercury/series?range=6h|24h|7d|all` and `GET /api/system/mercury/latest` (`src/lib/system/mercury.ts`, `MERCURY_API_URL` override, 8s AbortController timeout, 502 on outage) consumed via SWR (`src/hooks/useMercury.ts`, 60s). The view (`src/components/performance/`) is a hand-rolled SVG chart (no chart-lib dependency) — a "Closet Climate Strip" with two °F axes (left auto-fits ambient so closet variation stays legible, right carries hot die temps), a power-draw wash, Detail/Util progressive-disclosure layers, and a stat strip that doubles as legend + per-series visibility toggle + hover readout. Reachable via the navigate CLI (`{"view":"system","path":"/performance"}`).

- **Desktop app setup and bundle verification checks** — Added `npm run doctor:local` and `npm run verify:desktop`. The app build commands now run the doctor before building and the verifier after creating `dist/Hilt.app`, covering Node/npm major version, local-disk checkout, installed dependencies, Electron resolution, native launcher architecture, and app bundle structure.

- **Hilt rearchitecture proposal recovered** — Saved the pre-pull `Claude's Suggestion for Hilt Re-Architecture` document as `docs/plans/hilt-rearchitecture-proposal.md`, with provenance from the safety stash and corrected relative links for its new plans-folder location.

- **Goal-aware daily briefings and weekend editions** — Hilt now understands two briefing kinds in one Briefing list: weekday daily files at `briefings/YYYY-MM-DD.md` and weekend files at `briefings/weekend/YYYY-MM-DD.md` keyed as `weekend:YYYY-MM-DD`. Weekend rows display date-range labels in the existing dropdown, share the same renderer, and use id-based read state so weekend editions do not collide with daily dates. The Bridge briefing gatherer now injects a deterministic North Stars / Areas context block from `areas/index.md` plus compact area Goals, Standards, and Active Projects; prompt guidance treats goals as a relevance prior rather than a daily checklist. Hermes now runs Morning Briefing weekdays only and a new Weekend Briefing job Saturday/Sunday, with a scratch harness under `$HOME/.hilt/briefing-drafts/<date>/` for candidate validation.

- **Bridge Priorities now surfaces Areas of Focus** — The Priorities screen now reads the Bridge `areas/` structure through a new `/api/bridge/areas` endpoint and renders an Areas section below weekly tasks and above Writing. Areas display as a horizontal Now/Ongoing/Long-Term/Other board with domain-specific icons and visible `## Goals` bullets on each card instead of path/count metadata; cards participate in Bridge search and open the backing area markdown in Docs. The Bridge watcher now emits `areas-changed` so edits refresh like tasks, projects, thoughts, and people.

### Changed

- **Briefings UI collapsed to a single briefing (v1/v2/Compare era over — v2 IS the briefing)** — With the native generator cut over, the shadow-review comparison surface is gone: `BriefingsView` no longer has the `v1 | v2 | Compare` segmented control, the shadow fetch, or the split Compare layout — one `max-w-3xl` pane renders THE briefing, with loop escalations nested inside their owning sections (previously only the v2 shadow pane got the nesting) via a view-level `useEscalations()`. The whole-briefing feedback affordance survives the collapse: `ShadowFeedbackButton` → `BriefingFeedbackButton` (label "Feedback"), same `POST /api/loops/feedback` at `level=briefing`, now living in the header-right slot next to the Bridge mode toggle. `GET /api/bridge/briefings/shadow` is deleted.

- **Prose vertical rhythm tightened a notch, uniformly, via one knob** — Tailwind prose's default block spacing read a touch loose across both reading surfaces. Rather than tweak elements individually (which would flatten the calibrated rhythm), every block's vertical margin is now scaled by a single factor `--prose-rhythm` (currently `0.85`) in `globals.css`, hung off the `.hilt-prose.prose` marker that `SHARED_PROSE_TUNING` stamps — so Docs read-mode and Library both compact proportionally from one place, with prose's edge/post-heading resets preserved. Line-height and text sizing are untouched; dialing `--prose-rhythm` is the only lever.

- **Performance telemetry folded fully into Hilt (the standalone `mercury-observability` stack is retired)** — The Performance subtab no longer proxies to a separate Node project on `:8787`; Hilt now collects, stores, and serves the data itself, generalized to a **per-machine** model so any machine reporting telemetry just appears as another line (no hardcoded `<machine>_*` columns). New `src/lib/system/telemetry/`: `db.ts` (a `better-sqlite3` store at `${DATA_DIR}/metrics.sqlite` — `machine_samples` keyed `(ts, machine_id)`, `ambient_samples` keyed `ts` so closet/outdoor are stored once; WAL + additive migration, modeled on `granola/db.ts`), `local.ts` (`readLocalMetrics()` — macmon die temps/power + sysctl/vm_stat/top, plus a closet block read from the **local** Homebridge/SmartThings token on the owner machine; ports the old `thermal`/`localMetrics`/`smartthings` adapters with **no SSH**), `nws.ts` (outdoor via NWS, disk-cached), `daemon.ts` (in-process collector started by ws-server, gated by `HILT_METRICS_COLLECTOR=1`), `serve.ts` + `catalog.ts` (range query + machine→label/color catalog, stable colors with the collector first so Mercury=violet/Hestia=magenta are preserved). Each machine reports its own telemetry via `GET /api/system/metrics` — added to the **System Agent** allowlist (`server/system-agent.ts`, read-only, closet token never serialized) and as a full-Hilt self route. Serving moved from `/api/system/mercury/*` (deleted, along with `src/lib/system/mercury.ts`) to `/api/system/performance/{series,latest}`: the collector machine reads the local store; viewers proxy to it (`HILT_METRICS_SOURCE_URL`). The chart (`PerfChart.tsx`/`PerformanceView.tsx`, hook renamed `useMercury`→`usePerformance`) now generates one right-axis chip line per machine from the served catalog. Topology: **Mercury** (supervised, always-on) collects + stores + serves — `HILT_METRICS_COLLECTOR=1`/`HILT_METRICS_CLOSET_MACHINE=hestia` set only in its supervisor plist; **Hestia** runs the agent + holds the closet sensor (`HILT_METRICS_CLOSET=1` baked into its agent plist at install); **Apollo** and other viewers only read. Existing history is carried over by `scripts/metrics-import.ts` (`npm run metrics:import`).

- **Docs and Library now share one prose treatment (single source of truth)** — `DocsEditor.tsx` and `LibraryMarkdown.tsx` each carried a near-identical copy of the long Tailwind-Typography class string (font, `prose-headings:font-semibold`, and the whole code/pre/table tuning — ~70% duplicated), free to silently drift. That shared base is now `SHARED_PROSE_TUNING` in `src/lib/prose.ts`, composed by both. Legitimate per-surface deltas stay at each call site, documented: Docs keeps `leading-normal` + blue web-links; Library inherits prose's rhythm (no `leading-normal`, per §314) with app-token body colors, `prose-img`/`prose-hr`, and document-style links (§523). Because the class strings now live in a `.ts` module rather than inline in a component, `globals.css` pins it with `@source "../lib/prose.ts"` so Tailwind still generates those utilities (verified present in the built CSS). Net: no visual change to either surface — the shared 70% just can't drift apart anymore.

- **Library feed now orders by intake date ("first time I saw it"), not the source's publish date** — The feed sorted saved refs by `published` (and candidates by `published || digested`), so a months-old tweet or a week-old candidate bookmarked today sank to its publish position instead of surfacing at the top. The feed key is now the *intake* date: `referenceCreatedDate` prefers `saved_at`/`captured`/`captured_at` over `published` (falling back to `published` for legacy items written before intake stamping), and candidate `created_at` keys off `digested` (its always-stamped first-seen date) — which also reconciles the merged feed with candidate-cache's own `digested`-desc sort. For normal ingestion `captured≈published` (75/79 saved refs are within 3 days), so only deliberately-saved older content actually moves — e.g. a 2025-12-23 tweet captured 2026-06-15 now sits at June 15, and a freshly-promoted bookmark goes straight to the top. Pairs with the explicit-save→promote fix: bookmarking a discovered candidate both promotes it to a durable saved reference *and* re-dates it to the save moment.

- **Performance subtab now plots Hestia's chip temperature alongside Mercury's** — The chart's framing is "one closet, two heat sources": the right (chip °F) axis now carries two die-temp lines, **Mercury (violet)** and **Hestia (magenta)**, so you can see at a glance which machine is heating the shared closet. Required adding the data, which didn't exist before — Hestia (an M1 Mac mini) only ran the read-only System Agent, no telemetry. Rather than stand up a second observability stack, the existing **single Mercury collector was extended** (`/Users/jruck/projects/mercury-observability`): a new `lib/sources/hestiaThermal.mjs` adapter SSHes to Hestia and runs `macmon pipe` (the same sudoless IOReport reader Mercury uses on itself; `brew install macmon` on Hestia was the only new dependency), reusing the exact `execFile('ssh', …)` pattern `smartthings.mjs` already uses for the closet sensor. Two nullable columns `hestia_cpu_temp_c`/`hestia_gpu_temp_c` were added to `lib/db.mjs` `METRIC_COLUMNS` + `SCHEMA` (the existing `ensureColumns()` additive migration `ALTER`s the live SQLite table) and the adapter registered in `collector.mjs`'s concurrent timeout-bounded `SOURCES`. The M1 mini exposes no discrete GPU die sensor (macmon reports `gpu_temp_avg≈0`), so the adapter coerces sub-1°C readings to null and Hestia's line rides on CPU die temp. On the Hilt side the proxy is a generic JSON pass-through, so the new columns needed **no server change** — only `MercurySample` (`useMercury.ts`) gained the two fields and `PerfChart.tsx` gained a `hestiaCompute` series (max of the two → °F) on the right axis (which auto-fits to both chips). The stat strip renames "Compute" → "Mercury" and adds "Hestia"; both chip lines are solid, distinguished by hue (violet vs magenta) per the design choice.

- **Performance subtab reduced to a three-series closet-climate chart with dual auto-fit axes** — The Mercury Performance view dropped everything that wasn't a temperature: power-draw wash, GPU/Mem utilization, Load, Humidity, and the Detail/Util progressive-disclosure layers. Rationale: utilization/power are upstream proxies for the heat that *Compute* already expresses, leaving three °F series — Closet, Outdoor, Compute. They render on **two independent auto-fit axes**, each `niceDomain`-stretched to its own data so both fill the vertical space and overlap in screen space: **left (ambient)** carries Closet + Outdoor (human-range temps, where the 85/90 bands live); **right (chip, violet labels)** carries Compute, which runs ~40°F hotter and on a single shared axis crushed the ambient variation into a flat sliver. (An interim single-shared-axis version did exactly that — restoring per-axis normalization fixed it.) **Closet is the hero**: a thick line that **smoothly fades color by temperature** — solid green at/below 85°F, a continuous green→amber→red fade across the 85–90°F caution band, solid red at/above the 90°F ceiling. Implemented as per-color line *runs* (quantized to 0.5°F, one `<path>` per run, with boundary points carried so runs join seamlessly) rather than an SVG stroke gradient: the gradient approach mis-mapped because compute's range left the closet line in a thin slice that the `userSpaceOnUse` stroke gradient collapsed to a single (red) stop. Faint discrete zone **bands** back the 85/90 thresholds on the ambient axis (red fills from the ceiling to the top of that axis — compute is on its own axis now, so no wash) plus a labeled "90° ceiling" reference line. **Outdoor** is a faint pastel-blue filled backdrop (`fillOpacity 0.08`), bridged across gaps so its sparser sampling reads as a continuous wash. **Compute** is a thin violet line on the right axis. The stat strip collapses to the three series (closet's swatch tracks its live fade color). The temperature→color fn and thresholds live in `PerfChart.tsx` (`closetColor`/`CLOSET_WARN`/`CLOSET_CEILING`/`ZONE`). Data plumbing (Mercury proxy routes + SWR) is unchanged — this is purely the visualization layer.

- **X Article bookmarks are now classified as `x-article` at ingestion** — A bookmarked tweet whose only content is a `t.co` shortlink to an `x.com/i/article/<id>` URL *means* "save the article," but the X API can't read login-walled X Articles, so digestion landed it as a bare `format: tweet` metadata stub (correctly flagged `needs_refetch`/unfetched by capture-health). Digestion now detects the X Article share (`isXArticleUrl`), stamps the resolved article URL onto `metadata.x_article_url`, classifies it as `format: x-article` (a taxonomy format that previously existed but was never assigned to anything), and emits a clear note pointing at browser recovery instead of the generic "metadata-limited" message. This is the parsing-side half: the article *body* still has to be filled by a browser recovery pass (the API fundamentally can't fetch it).

- **X content recovery ported from the dead `browser-use` CLI to `browser-harness`** — `scripts/library-x-recover.ts` shelled out to a `browser-use` CLI that is no longer installed on the recovery host (Mercury now runs `browser-harness`), so recovery had been silently inoperative. It now drives `browser-harness` (pipes a Python snippet on stdin; `new_tab`/`js`/`cdp` helpers attach to the running signed-in Chrome — override the binary with `BROWSER_HARNESS_BIN`). The extractor now **waits for the X Article view to actually paint** (`[data-testid=twitterArticleRichTextView]`) before trusting a read, instead of breaking on the first ≥800-char hit — which was returning page nav/footer chrome that the login-wall gate then (correctly) rejected. `contentUrlFor` also prefers the new `x_article_url` frontmatter stamp before falling back to the body-link regex. Verified end to end against a real X Article (pulled 14k chars of body text); still **manual-only** (drives the live browser) and still needs the one-time CDP authorize (Allow on `chrome://inspect`) on the recovery host. Unattended/auto recovery via a synced cloud profile remains the open follow-up.

- **Library list parsing is now memoized per file** — `parseReferenceFile` and `parseCandidateFile` previously re-ran the full transform (regex Summary/Key Points/Connections extraction, tag derivation, object construction) for every one of ~1000 reference + candidate markdown files on **every** `/api/library` request, just to return a 50-card page. Both now cache the derived object keyed on `mtimeMs+size` — the same proven pattern `parseMarkdownFile` already uses one layer down for the raw gray-matter parse. Any write (in-place edit or atomic temp+rename) changes the stat and invalidates exactly the touched file, so no manual cache-busting is needed; sharing the cached object is safe because the read path is mutation-free. Measured on the live vault via `library:metrics`: list **p50 194ms → 83ms**, **p95 391ms → 126ms**. The residual list cost is no longer file parsing — warm `listLibraryArtifactDetails(50)` is ~10ms — it is the per-card eval scoring (`scoreArtifacts` decorating each card with `eval_attrs`, ~1.3ms × 50). Recommendations (~795ms) are unchanged because they are scoring-bound (`evaluateLibrary` scores all ~1000 items, ~753ms), not load-bound; that is a separate score-cache effort.

- **Library reader links now behave like document links, not blue web chrome** — Library markdown links are always underlined in the same primary prose color as strong/header text, without becoming bold. Hover now affects only the individual link underline instead of underlining every link when the article pane is hovered, and markdown separators use the neutral border token rather than inheriting a blue accent.

- **Library saved/candidate lifecycle controls are now visually distinct and shared** — Feed cards and the detail reader now use one lifecycle menu component: candidates show an amber dashed-circle state with Save/Dismiss, while saved references show a filled green check-circle with source/unread/archive actions. Saved-reference archive moved out of the generic overflow menu so the action sits with the saved lifecycle state it changes.

- **Agent instructions clarify prod rebuild responsibility** — `AGENTS.md` now matches `CLAUDE.md` on the prod daily-driver workflow (`npm run app:prod`, `npm run rebuild`, supervisor status) and both files explicitly require agents to run `npm run rebuild` after user-visible app code changes unless the change is docs/test-only or the user says not to.

- **Library nav dot = "new since you last looked," not "unread exists"** — The top-nav Library dot was driven by `hasUnreadLibraryArtifacts` (any item not yet individually read), which is perma-on under steady ingestion — useless as a signal. It now means *items arrived since you last opened the Library tab*: a single `last_visited_at` timestamp on the read-state, with `isLibraryArtifactNew` (arrival-time vs. last-visit, independent of per-item read state) and `hasNewLibraryArtifacts`. `GET /api/library/unread` returns `has_new` (with `has_unread` kept as a back-compat alias); a new `POST` marks the tab visited. Board stamps the visit (optimistically clearing the dot) whenever the Library view opens, via a stable `markVisited` from `useLibraryUnread`. Per-item unread dots on feed cards are unchanged — this only re-defines the nav-level signal.

### Added

- **ⓘ reference: full real paths everywhere + storage clarity + two navigation bugs fixed** — Every link in HOW-IT-WORKS now shows the complete path it opens (the API expands `$VAULT`/`$DATA`/`$HILT` tokens in visible text, not just hrefs), and a new "Where things physically live" section answers the sandbox question head-on: exactly two storage roots (the vault; Hilt's private `~/.hilt/data` outside git) bridged by two git-ignored symlinks (`meta/loops-shadow`, `meta/briefing-shadow`) that exist purely so Docs can inspect sandbox files. Fixed en route: (1) Board's view-prefs hydration effect had `urlViewMode` in its deps, so EVERY navigation re-ran it and re-opened the ⓘ pane from stale localStorage — defeating both close paths; HUD/pane visibility now hydrates once at mount. (2) Navigation now closes the pane structurally (effect on scope/view change) rather than relying on individual click handlers. Verified end-to-end: doc link → pane closes → Docs opens the symlinked ledger with content rendered.

- **HOW-IT-WORKS rewritten around the node/fractal model (Justin's framing)** — One pattern stated once (scope → synthesis artifact → state/verdicts/feedback drawers → escalations up, in two flavors: know-this vs decide-this), then the tree: briefing at top, meetings/library/goals/system beneath, goals shown honestly as a roll-up node reading the meeting ledger sideways, the library shown as a sub-team (intake/synthesis/upkeep workers — the fractal's clearest example), raw feeds (calendar/tasks/git) marked as the no-node-yet gap where dormant loops (people-projections, calendar-tasks) slot in, and the briefing itself flagged as "half a node" (feedback drawer, no artifact/health). Full file inventory and open:// links preserved. Accuracy pass: all 26 links verified on disk; every schedule/behavior claim traced to plists or code.

- **In-app "How it all works" reference (ⓘ in the top bar)** — A new Info toggle in the NavBar (left of the source dropdown) swaps the content area for a rendered view of `docs/HOW-IT-WORKS.md`: the canonical plain-language walkthrough of the loops → artifacts → editor → verdicts flywheel, grouped by loop, with every referenced file/folder as an `open://` link that opens directly in the Docs view (`/api/system/how-it-works` expands `$VAULT`/`$DATA`/`$HILT` placeholders at request time). CLAUDE.md now mandates updating the doc whenever loops, schedules, the briefing pipeline, or file locations change — it renders in-app, so staleness is a user-facing bug.

### Changed

- **Briefings v2 morning surface restructured to scope (Justin's first-look feedback, 2026-07-02 night)** — Five connected changes after the first real look at the surface: (1) review tabs renamed `v1 | v2 | Compare` ("Live" was wrong — both briefings generate live each morning) and **v2 is now the default** when a shadow exists; (2) the escalations fold moved off the v1 pane and into the v2 pane (and Compare's v2 column) — scope §4: the top fold belongs to the loops briefing, "do not build a separate escalation-queue system"; (3) the fold is grouped, not flat: meeting asks group by SOURCE MEETING behind collapsed counts ("Needs you — 40 asks from 5 meetings · 3 signals"), runtime/goals signals stay flat, newest meeting first; (4) **feedback on every briefing item** (scope §6's universal comment affordance): hover any bullet → comment icon → inline input, anchored by (section, bullet text) and routed to the briefing loop — `/api/loops/feedback` now accepts the disabled briefing loop at every level during shadow, not just whole-briefing; (5) `BriefingContent` renderer no longer drops non-bullet lines — the day-thesis lede, prose-styled sections (Library appeared completely empty), and standalone report-link lines all render now; parsing stops at the `---` footer rule. Data-layer companions: meeting-loop aging redefined (only APPROVED commitments age-escalate, capped 5/run — un-verdicted backfill had re-flooded the panel via the aging path), on top of the earlier recent-only escalation gate and recent-first queue priority.

### Changed (UI)

- **ⓘ reference pane now persists across refresh, like the HUD** — The info pane's open state was ephemeral (`useState` only), so a refresh dropped it while the HUD survived. It's a mode of the app, not transient chrome (new DESIGN-PHILOSOPHY principle: persistent surfaces vs. ephemeral chrome), so `Board.tsx` now hydrates/persists `howItWorksOpen` via localStorage (`hilt-how-it-works-open`), exactly mirroring the `HUD_VISIBILITY_STORAGE_KEY` pattern (hydrate in the mount effect, persist gated on `isHydrated`).

### Fixed

- **Link hover no longer lights up every link in the pane (ⓘ reference, briefings, escalations, Docs read-mode)** — `hover:prose-a:*` compiles to *container*-hover (`.prose:hover a`), so hovering anywhere in the pane underlined/recolored **all** links. Replaced with the per-link arbitrary variant `[&_a:hover]:*` in all four components that used it (`HowItWorksDoc`, `BriefingContent` ×2, `EscalationsPanel`, `DocsEditor`) — same fix the Library reader got earlier via `.library-markdown a` CSS; this closes out the remaining prose surfaces.

- **Docs can now navigate to folders that have no index file** — Linking/navigating to a directory without `index.md` previously just deselected everything: no tree highlight, no scroll, stale/blank content pane — the link appeared broken. Now the folder itself gets selected: ancestors expand, the folder row highlights and scrolls into view (new `scrollIntoView` on selected tree rows — benefits file navigation too), and the content pane shows a folder placeholder ("This folder has no preview — select a file inside it to view"), mirroring the unviewable-file fallback. Implemented as a `selectedDirPath` state in `DocsView` (cleared whenever a real file is selected) threaded to `DocsFileTree` (highlight) and `DocsContentPane` (new `directoryPath` prop). Folders *with* an index still open it, unchanged. **Follow-up (same day): symlinked folders were invisible to the tree entirely** — `Dirent.isDirectory()`/`isFile()` are both false for symlinks, so the walker silently dropped e.g. the vault's `meta/loops-shadow` → `~/.hilt` sandbox links (which exist precisely to keep that data inspectable in Docs); navigating to one fell into the file branch and dead-ended on "path must be a file, not a directory". The tree walker now resolves each entry's effective type through the link (`statSync`; broken links skipped; cycles bounded by `MAX_DEPTH`), so symlinked dirs/files list, sort, and browse like real ones — verified live (`loops-shadow`/`briefing-shadow` now in the tree with sandbox contents). Plus a resilience net in `DocsView`: any selected path that errors as a directory converts to the folder-selection experience instead of a dead error pane.

- **HUD agenda rows no longer crop at the bottom** — The HUD's panel grid never declared a row, so the single implicit row auto-sized to *content*: when the agenda (Today + Tomorrow tasks/events) exceeded the fixed HUD height, panels overflowed and the bottom row was clipped by `overflow-hidden` instead of the agenda list scrolling. Added `grid-rows-[minmax(0,1fr)]` to all four grid variants so panels are pinned to the container height and the inner `overflow-y-auto` list actually scrolls.

- **Fenced code blocks no longer render dark-on-light (ⓘ reference pane and every prose surface)** — Tailwind Typography's default `pre` is a *fixed dark slate* (`--tw-prose-pre-bg`) regardless of app theme, so any markdown surface composed without `SHARED_PROSE_TUNING` showed black code boxes in light mode — most visibly the ⓘ HOW-IT-WORKS pane's ASCII trees. Fixed systemically, two layers: (1) a `globals.css` safety net pins every `.prose pre` (+ `pre code`) to theme tokens (`--bg-tertiary`/`--text-secondary`) — plain `.prose pre` specificity (0,1,1) outranks prose's zero-specificity `:where()` rules, so this catches all six surfaces that use `prose` without the shared tuning (HowItWorksDoc, BriefingContent, EscalationsPanel, XPostEmbed, VideoTranscript, MeetingEntry) and any future escapee; (2) `HowItWorksDoc` now composes `SHARED_PROSE_TUNING` like Docs/Library (the intended pattern for full-document surfaces), keeping only its surface deltas (compact heading scale, app-token body colors, interactive links).

- **Runtime loop disk warning now follows macOS/Finder available space** — The Briefings v2 runtime loop no longer escalates Mercury's disk solely from `df` free blocks, which can show ~8% on APFS while Finder reports much more reclaimable/available space. The scheduled runner now uses `NSURLVolumeAvailableCapacityForImportantUsageKey` on macOS and falls back to `df` elsewhere; the loop artifact still records the lower immediate `df` free percentage as diagnostic context.

- **Monday-morning triple failure: asks aged out undecided, v2 had no retry net, and two validator rules fought each other** — (1) The 3-day escalation recency gate silently dropped 15 UNDECIDED asks over the holiday weekend; policy fixed: recency admits an ask to the queue, but once in it stays until decided (`first_escalated_at` stamped on the ledger entry; June backfill that never met the bar stays latent). (2) The 06:00 v1 failure was healed by the weekday retry watcher at 10:54 while v2's identical failure sat dead all day (no toggle, no asks) — the watcher now retries BOTH briefings. (3) The memo-link rule kept rejecting honest drafts: it fired on the bold day-thesis lede (now exempt — links there violate house style anyway) and it demanded the link inline on the featured line while the LINKS rule mandates standalone link lines (now: same line OR the immediately-following line). Also: Board's first render gated on a requestAnimationFrame tick — a frame-starved context (occluded/background/headless) never fires RAF and the whole app rendered null; hydration now falls back to an 80ms timeout.

- **Weekend validator floor rejected honest holiday briefings** — July 4th weekend produced two independent ~3.5KB weekend drafts and the 4000B floor failed both, leaving NO live weekend briefing (and since the briefing list is built from vault files, the UI showed no July 4 entry at all — hiding a perfectly valid v2 shadow). The floor's job is catching truncation/derailment (<2KB, e.g. the 969B commentary breach), not arguing with CALIBRATION's "thin day = short briefing" rule; weekend floor now 2200 (same as daily). Third generation passed at 4244B and committed. Known remaining gap (D-003): the briefing retry watcher is weekday-only, and the runtime loop runs at 5:45 — BEFORE the 6:00/6:20 briefing jobs — so a weekend briefing failure isn't caught by anything until the next morning.

- **Shadow briefing API looked in the wrong directory (Compare surface was dead on arrival)** — `GET /api/bridge/briefings/shadow` joined `parseBriefingId().relativePath` (which includes the vault's `briefings/` prefix) onto `$DATA_DIR/briefing-shadow/`, but the shadow generator strips that prefix (dailies flat, weekends under `weekend/` — `scripts/briefing-generate.ts --shadow`). Every lookup 404'd → `hasShadow` stayed false → the `Live | v2 shadow | Compare` toggle never rendered. The route now strips the prefix to mirror the generator. Caught by the pre-launch UI verification pass; verified live for both a daily and a weekend shadow.

- **Goals loop retro runs no longer see future ledger entries** — `observedLedger()` read the current open action ledger regardless of `--as-of`, so a retro of a historical week could cite ledger entries opened weeks later (the same future-state confound that poisoned briefing grading round 1). As-of runs now filter to entries `opened_at <= until`. Also added `--evidence-dump <path>` so retro/refuter passes can grade the loop's claims against exactly the evidence bundle the model saw (the launchpad `gather.txt` pattern).

- **Summarize CLI flag drift broke L1 digests wholesale (every tweet + all live source extraction)** — The `summarize` CLI was upgraded to 0.9.0, which **removed/renamed flags Hilt still passed** — `--force-summary`, `--max-extract-characters`, `--timestamps`, `--slides`/`--slides-max`. summarize hard-rejects unknown options (`error: unknown option '--force-summary'` → exit 1), and `runSummarize` swallowed the error to `null`, so two whole paths silently died: `summarizeText` (the cached-text/fallback digest — the **only** L1 path for tweets, since X URLs are login-walled and skip `summarizeUrl`) and `extractSourceContent` (live URL/YouTube source extraction, which always passed `--max-extract-characters`). The visible symptom: freshly-ingested tweets fell back to the crude **structural** digest — Summary = "first 4 sentences verbatim" (truncating mid-enumeration), Key Points = "whatever bullets exist in the source" — so a tweet listing five role archetypes summarized as a cut-off prose dump (the user's Boris Cherny example). Fix: dropped the dead flags (the char cap now applies in code via `slice`, not a CLI flag; `--video-mode transcript` is retained — it's still valid), and `runSummarize` now **warns loudly on an "unknown option" stderr** (once) so a future CLI drift surfaces instead of silently degrading the whole library. Verified: with the flags reconciled, summarize produces a clean digest that enumerates all five archetypes (`google/gemini-3.5-flash`, ~$0.01). Study items flagged `reweave_pending` self-heal on the (now-authenticated) nightly reweave; this also restores YouTube/article source extraction, which had been fully dead.

- **Raw video transcripts can no longer masquerade as the digest (the "it just dumped the raw content" failure)** — For some videos the `summarize` CLI returns the *verbatim transcript* (YouTube `--video-mode transcript`, often led by a literal `Transcript:` label) instead of a summary. Digestion used that output as the body unconditionally (`digestMarkdown = summarized`), so the whole transcript landed as the "digest": the description was derived from spoken-word noise, and the file ballooned to 50–112k chars. That bloat then **starved the very reweave that would fix it** — a 100k+ body makes the connection pass's vault exploration time out, so the item could never self-heal (the symptom the user flagged on the Fiona Fung and ViralBench items: "didn't summarize," "just dumped the raw content"). Fix: a new guard `looksLikeRawTranscriptDump()` in `digestion.ts` detects a `Transcript:`-led or very-long-and-structureless "digest", treats it as a **failed L1 digest** (drops it so summary/key-points fall back to the structural source text), and flags `reweave_pending` so a later pass writes a real digest — exactly the graceful-degradation path already used for rate-limited reweaves. Swept the existing library for the same shape: 4 video items carried a transcript-as-digest (one flagged `reweave_pending`, three silently `pending=false` so the nightly was ignoring them); all were rebuilt to a small file (iframe-only `## Media`, the transcript moved into a capped `## Raw Content` source cache) and re-flagged for reweave. New unit tests in `library.test.ts`. Also confirmed `summarize-cli` now has a provider key (Gemini, sourced from Hestia and exported by `hilt-launchd-npm.sh` from `~/.summarize/config.json`), so scheduled L1 digests run instead of degrading to a metadata stub.

- **Scheduled reweave now authenticates with the OAuth token, not the stale Keychain** — Every nightly reweave (and the For You editor pass) was failing — "Reweave did not update the file" — so saved items piled up as raw L1 dumps with no real digest (47 items backlogged; the symptom the user kept hitting: "the quality of the summary is just missing"). Root cause: on macOS, Claude Code **prefers the login Keychain over `CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN`** (verified: a bogus token + valid Keychain still authenticates), and the Keychain's short-lived access token can't refresh in a headless launchd context at 03:35 → every scheduled `claude -p` 401s. The token we wired in (`hilt-launchd-npm.sh`) was being ignored. Fix: `forcedTokenEnv` in `connections.ts` runs the headless `claude` subprocess with a **minimal env** (allowlist: PATH/HOME/TMPDIR/lang/token) when `CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN` is set, stripping whatever lets Claude reach the Keychain so it's forced onto the token — verified by reweaving ViralBench + the Claire Vo talk cleanly through the production path. Interactive runs (no token) keep the full env + Keychain, unchanged. Drains the whole reweave backlog. (Separately noted: `summarize-cli` has no provider API key, so the pre-reweave L1 placeholder is degraded — the reweave is the real quality producer; wiring summarize to a key/CLI provider is a follow-up.)

- **PDFs are extracted to text instead of dumped as binary garbage** — A PDF uploaded to Raindrop (a `Loop-Engineering-IEEE.pdf` bookmark) landed with its `## Raw Content` cache full of `%PDF` binary — unreadable, and ~43% of bytes corrupted because `fetchRaindropCache` read the file with `response.text()` (UTF-8). With no real text, nothing summarized and the item never wove. Now digestion reads the cache as **bytes** (`arrayBuffer`), detects PDFs (content-type or `%PDF` magic), and extracts prose with `pdftotext` (poppler; `PDFTOTEXT_BIN` override) via the new `src/lib/library/pdf.ts` — `extractor: "raindrop-pdf"`, `kind: "document"`. Direct `.pdf` URLs from any source go through the same path (`extractSourceContent` → `fetchPdfUrlText`) rather than scraping a viewer page. A binary backstop (`looksLikeBinaryGarbage` in capture-health, wired into `captureFailed`) ensures undecodable bytes can never land as — or survive as — a cached source again. Confirmed end to end: the Loop-Engineering paper now reads as a clean 9,661-word extraction → full digest + connections; a vault scan found **0** other binary-garbage items.

- **Reweave no longer preserves a raw-cache wall stuck under `## Media`** — When a prior digest was a heading-less wall of text (a failed summarize that dumped raw cache directly under Media with no `## ` of its own), `library-reweave.ts` preserved the "Media section verbatim" using *everything from `## Media` to the next `## ` heading* — which swallowed the entire wall as "media" and carried it forward, leaving it stuck above the clean rewoven digest. A new `extractMediaSection` keeps only the leading media block (images/embeds) and stops at the first prose line. A vault scan found exactly one already-polluted item (the Medallia article, the only piece both login-walled and rewoven-after-failure); re-reweaving it with the fix produced a clean Media → digest body. Future reweaves of any failed-digest backlog item are protected.

- **Login-walled Raindrop captures now summarize from the cache instead of dumping a wall of text** — A LinkedIn (or any login-walled) article bookmarked via Raindrop landed broken: the reader's Summary was identical to the raw cache dump (sign-in chrome → article → comments → nav → language picker), the description was login boilerplate, and it was graded `digestion_status: hot`. Root cause: `digestArtifact` ran the summarizer on the live URL (login wall → null) and on the short Raindrop *excerpt* (skipped, <400 chars), then fetched the full ~26k Raindrop cache **after** the summarizer had already given up — so the real article never reached it and the "summary" fell back to the first sentences of the cache (the sign-in chrome). Digestion now acquires the source (live extract → Raindrop permanent copy → source-metadata) **before** the text-summarize fallback and runs the summarizer on the full acquired content (`digestion.ts`); a chrome-only live extract is dropped so the Raindrop cache takes over. Verified: the Medallia item reweaves to a clean 5-section digest + real description from the cache.

- **Login-wall detection so chrome-only captures aren't graded "hot"** — New `loginWallVerdict(text)` in `capture-health.ts` (shared phrase set + a prose-word threshold, env `LIBRARY_LOGIN_WALL_MIN_PROSE_WORDS`, default 50) distinguishes "sign-in gate with a real article underneath" (the common Raindrop case → clean + summarize + weave normally) from "bare sign-in wall" (→ never `hot`; stamped `needs_auth_recovery` and excluded from reweave via `captureFailed`, routed to authenticated recovery). A regression scan of 979 refs/candidates flagged **0** existing items, confirming the threshold doesn't over-trigger.

- **Library eval no longer shows a contradictory substance signal** — The inspection panel showed "substance graded: no" beside a confident "substance 85". The substance score is a *structural estimate* (format + length) until a model grades it at reweave; the panel now labels the ungraded value "… · est." with an explanatory tooltip (`LibraryArtifactDetailPane.tsx`).

- **"Copy session ID" now works** — The System ▸ Map session-copy called `navigator.clipboard.writeText` with no fallback, so it failed silently in contexts where the async Clipboard API is unavailable. It now routes through the shared `copyToClipboard` (textarea fallback) and copies a full session reference (externalId + provider + title + workspace) instead of the bare internal id.

- **Library reader rhythm now matches Docs read-mode (the gold master)** — `LibraryMarkdown` applied `leading-normal` (line-height 1.5) over Tailwind `prose`, which tightened body lines while prose's generous heading margins stayed put — an uneven "tight paragraphs / big section gaps" rhythm that read as hand-tuned spacing. Per DESIGN-PHILOSOPHY §314 (Docs read-mode is the typographic gold master, and Docs relies on prose's calibrated defaults), the override is removed so body line-height and heading spacing now come from the same prose rhythm Docs uses. The remaining `prose-*` utilities only map colors to theme tokens; structure/spacing/sizing are prose's job, not micromanaged per element.

- **Explicit bookmarks of already-discovered items are now honored (no longer dropped)** — `processArtifact` checked for an existing discovery candidate and returned `duplicate` *before* the `explicit_save` branch, so bookmarking something a discovery source (e.g. a YouTube channel feed) had already surfaced as a candidate silently dropped the explicit intent — the item stayed a TTL-expiring candidate and never became a durable saved reference. This was the root cause of "I bookmarked it but the library never pulled it in" when the URL overlapped a followed source. An `explicit_save` whose URL matches an existing candidate now **promotes** that candidate to a durable reference via `promoteCandidate` (`reason: explicit_save_promoted_candidate`; dry-run reports `dry_run_explicit_promote`). Confirmed against the YC video "The Age Of The 40-Year-Old Solo Founder Is Here" (`8OOuCnZB-4o`), discovered via `youtube-ycombinator` then bookmarked.

- **Scheduled (launchd) Claude jobs no longer 401 overnight** — Interactive Claude Code stores its OAuth in the macOS Keychain, which a launchd job's process cannot reliably reach/refresh; on Mercury this made headless `claude -p` (the nightly `reweave-pending` drain and the `recommendations`/editor-pass job) fail with `401 Invalid authentication credentials` every night, stalling enrichment and the For You feed (Hestia was immune only because it used file-based creds). `scripts/hilt-launchd-npm.sh` now exports a long-lived `CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN` (minted via `claude setup-token`, stored unquoted in gitignored `.env.local`) so every scheduled job and its child `claude` inherit it, bypassing the Keychain. Both `library-reweave.ts` and `library-editor-pass.ts` already `loadEnvConfig`, so the token also flows through that path.

- **For You editor pass exits clean on an API 401 instead of ambering the health panel** — The catch-block envelope detector required an `api_error_status` field, but a 401 arrives as `is_error:true` with the code only in the result string (`API Error: 401 …`), so it fell through to `throw` and dumped the entire prompt to stderr — flagging the `recommendations` scheduler job as a warning for a designed-for miss. It now matches the `API Error: <code>` / generic `is_error:true` shapes too, logging a compact `{skipped:"api_error"}` and falling back to the cached/deterministic picks as intended.

- **Resolved library dead-letters are now pruned so the health panel reflects live problems** — A 2-hour credential outage (2026-06-19, since self-recovered) left ~150 resolved dead-letter entries whose by-source counts kept showing in Library Health as if active. `pruneResolvedDeadLetters` (entries resolved by a later source success or the artifact now existing in storage) now runs as part of the nightly `cleanup` job and reports `pruned_dead_letters`.

- **Editor's memo article mentions now open native Library items** — The latest memo was backfilled with Hilt wikilinks for saved references and active candidates mentioned in the prose. Future `library:memo` runs now ask Claude to emit `[[path|title]]` links for referenced intake items and run a deterministic post-pass over the returned `referenced_items` manifest to link any plain title mentions that still resolve in Library.

- **Library memo dates now survive machine migration timestamps** — Saved references now honor `created_at`, `captured_at`, `saved_at`, `digested_at`, and `fetched_at` frontmatter before falling back to filesystem birthtime. This fixes migrated editor's memos appearing with the Mercury copy date even though their memo frontmatter carried the real generation dates.

- **Library X recovery no longer accepts login-wall boilerplate as source text** — `library:x:recover` now rejects X login/signup/footer copy such as "Continue with Apple", "By continuing, you agree…", and "Download the X app" before replacing a reference's Raw Content. This keeps Mercury browser-profile misses from falsely clearing `unfetched` X Article cards; the bad local recovery writes from the audit were restored from Xochipilli before retrying.

- **Hilt source app no longer bakes or silently falls back to absolute project paths** — `scripts/create-dev-app.sh` now recreates `dist/Hilt.app` cleanly, keeps the launcher C source out of the bundle, resolves the checkout from the app's `dist/` location at runtime, rejects `/Volumes` source launches with a clear dialog, prefers the `.nvmrc` Node 22 runtime, and fails fast when Electron or native modules are missing instead of creating a bundle that only fails after double-click.

- **Hilt.app no longer prompts for Rosetta on Apple Silicon without Rosetta installed** — The daily-driver app bundle now gives LaunchServices a native Mach-O `Contents/MacOS/launcher` executable instead of a script as `CFBundleExecutable`. The native stub execs the adjacent `launcher.sh`, preserving the existing project self-location, PATH discipline, and dev/prod mode bake while avoiding macOS classifying the app launch path as Intel-only before Electron starts. Rebuilt `dist/Hilt.app` verifies both the stub and Electron are `arm64`.

- **Hilt launchd scheduler jobs now use the supervisor Node runtime** — Library and Semantic calendar jobs now launch through `scripts/hilt-launchd-npm.sh`, mirroring the headless supervisor's nvm-first PATH discipline. This prevents Mercury's scheduled jobs from resolving Homebrew Node 26 while the supervised Hilt server and native modules are running under the nvm Node 22 runtime. Scheduler installs also accept `--only` / `--skip` job filters so a host cutover can install recurring Semantic jobs without firing the one-time `cold-start` backfill.

- **Granola sync no longer dirties Bridge markdown with runtime timestamps** — Meeting notes and transcript frontmatter no longer write `hilt_synced_at`; Bridge markdown keeps stable Granola/calendar provenance fields only, while operational sync timing remains in Hilt's local Granola DB (`last_synced_at`). The markdown writer also strips legacy `hilt_synced_at` if an old file is rewritten. Added regression tests that repeated writes with unchanged source content/provenance are no-ops, and removed 1,345 existing `hilt_synced_at` lines from tracked Bridge markdown as a one-time cleanup.

- **Briefing report links now stay inside Hilt** — Briefing markdown links to `/api/reports/memo` and `/api/reports/morning` now resolve through a native-link route before navigation. Editor's memo links open the matching memo as a Library item, and full Library report links open the dated markdown report in Docs, avoiding the raw Tailnet-served HTML report window.

- **Bridge nav remembers Briefing vs. Priorities while preserving the default** — The primary Bridge tab now restores the last Bridge subview (`Briefing` or `Priorities`) from localStorage when returning from Calendar, People, Library, Docs, or System. A missing preference still defaults to Briefing, while explicit switches and task-entry shortcuts update the remembered Bridge mode.

- **Calendar mini-months default open on desktop without ignoring user choice** — The Calendar tab now treats a missing mini-month preference as desktop-visible by default, while preserving explicit user toggles in localStorage so a manual hide stays hidden across refreshes.

- **Library X/article capture failures now stay honest and recover cleanly** — Capture health now reads only the `## Raw Content` section when deciding whether a `source-metadata` item is a real capture, so later `## Source Notes` cannot make a t.co/X Article stub look gradable. Feed cards and the detail metadata header render failed captures as amber `unfetched` instead of a normal worth score, and the metadata panel carries the `needs refetch` lifecycle. The browser-backed `library:x:recover` path now rejects `Author/Published/Links` stubs, prefers real X article/post DOM text, replaces the Raw Content section instead of appending around Source Notes, keeps richer browser-recovered article text when the direct tweet API only returns wrapper metadata, and clears stale connection/attention/substance judgments before marking `reweave_pending`. Backfill run: 43 X/article stubs found; 28 recovered including `references/2026-06-16-factory-2-0-from-coding-agents-to-software-factories.md`; 15 remain explicitly unresolved/unfetched; the Factory example was reweaved from the recovered article and now has 4 connections plus a fresh high `attention_judgment`.

- **Calendar/HUD event actions no longer show Zoom registration cruft as many links** — Calendar link extraction now recognizes Zoom webinar join URLs, filters generated Zoom registration email chrome such as add-to-calendar links, static images, and unsubscribe URLs, and suppresses provider buttons when the URL is just a meeting/generated action. Zoom registration confirmation text is also hidden from compact event detail previews.

- **Library feed cards no longer overlap after media settles** — Virtualized feed rows now use a measured row wrapper with a per-row `ResizeObserver` and animation-frame measurement, so late-loading thumbnails and embeds update the virtualizer's row heights instead of letting later cards keep stale positions.

- **Bridge task drag no longer rewrites from partial lists** — Reordering tasks now sends the viewed week to the backend and the weekly parser rejects reorder payloads that do not include every task exactly once, preventing filtered or stale drag state from deleting omitted tasks. The Bridge list now appends done/review tasks to reorder saves and disables drag handles while search is active, so a filtered task subset cannot become the entire markdown task section.

- **Bridge task drops no longer snap back before saving** — The task list now holds the dropped local order as the visible intent while the reorder mutation writes markdown and revalidates SWR, only releasing the local order after success or rollback. The optimistic reorder also preserves pre-save task IDs until the server reparse returns, avoiding stale drag container IDs during the in-flight state.

- **Bridge drag animation is more consistent in both directions** — Bridge priorities now use center-based collision detection, continuous droppable measuring, and flex gaps instead of margin-based `space-y` inside sortable groups. Pending saves disable only drag handles, not the sortable registrations themselves, so neighboring rows no longer unregister/reappear and flash after a drop.

- **Mobile Bridge/Briefing gutters are tighter** — The main Bridge and Briefing content shells now use smaller left/right padding on mobile while keeping the wider tablet/desktop gutter, so their content aligns more closely with the App HUD's mobile density.

- **X video bookmarks now capture transcripts instead of grading wrapper tweets** — X/Twitter video URLs are now first-class Library source content. `digestArtifact` detects `video_url` from bookmark entities, attached X media, linked X posts, and legacy Raw Content links; `src/lib/library/x-video-transcript.ts` uses `yt-dlp` subtitles first and falls back to downloaded-audio transcription via `summarize` when captions are absent. Successful captures write `cached_source_extractor: x-video-subtitles` or `x-video-audio`, persist `video_url`, `source_recovered_from`, and transcript status/method, and summarize/reweave from the transcript instead of tweet metadata. Missing transcript on an X video is a capture-health failure unless the video is explicitly terminal (`unavailable_no_audio` for silent media, `unavailable_source` for suspended/private/deleted media), so wrapper tweets no longer get confident scores when the actual video was unread. Added `npm run library:x:videos` for report-first backfills. One-time run: 9 historical X-video refs checked, 7 transcribed including `references/process/2026-06-12-good-interview.md`; 2 marked terminal unavailable (silent Buehler demo, suspended LED clip); follow-up dry run reports 0 unhandled X-video transcript misses.

- **Library tab activation now refreshes stale feed data** — Switching back into Library now revalidates the cached feed, source/facet counts, recommendations, review queue, and open detail records while preserving the stale-while-refresh UI. Hourly-ingested items no longer require a manual refresh or full page reload to appear after leaving another tab.

- **Library Health no longer warns on successful refetch recovery progress** — The System → Sync scheduler panel now treats `[refetch] RECOVERED …` stderr lines as benign scheduler progress, matching the refetch drain's stdout summary and exit code. Failed refetch outcomes such as `STILL_FAILED` remain actionable warnings.

- **Briefing links use Hilt interaction styling instead of blue** — Briefing markdown links now use `interactive-default`/`interactive-hover` with the same quiet no-underline-until-hover behavior as Docs read mode, rather than hardcoded blue Tailwind utilities.

- **Briefing bold contrast restored without a new body style** — Normal briefing bullet copy now uses the existing secondary text color while inline `strong` remains primary/semibold, making emphasis legible without introducing another global prose treatment.

- **Briefing cards no longer look selectable** — Briefing content and failure cards now use a static `hilt-card` variant that keeps the shared content surface without changing border on hover. Expand affordances remain on the actual expandable bullet rows, while Library-style card hover stays reserved for card-level selection/navigation.

- **Compact date labels no longer shout** — The shared Hilt display-date helper keeps shortened labels (`Fri, Jun 12`, `Jun 8 – 14`) but preserves normal `Intl.DateTimeFormat` casing. App HUD and Calendar compact weekday labels now follow the same normal-case rule instead of forcing all caps.

- **Reference Library metadata truth for connection passes** — The detail metadata panel now acts like a compact pipeline DevTools surface: it shows connection-pass state, evidence markers (`connection_suggestions`, `reconnected_at`, `connection_reasoning`, `attention_judgment`), the v2.2 `attention_judgment` tier/reason, connection output, reweave candidates, and missing-pass warnings. The shared connection-state helper now treats `attention_judgment` as positive evidence that the reweave pass ran, so clean no-connection abstentions no longer show as `0 · never` or queue as `missing_connection_pass`. Fresh ingestion also stamps `reconnected_at` and an explicit no-durable-connections reasoning on successful abstentions, and empty/unparseable reweave results no longer suppress `reweave_pending`.

- **Granola sync daemon restored under the headless supervisor** — The old launchd dev wrapper exported `HILT_GRANOLA_SYNC_DAEMON=1`, but the new `com.hilt.supervisor` wrapper did not, so the supervised app-server/ws-server stayed healthy while the Granola background worker quietly stopped after cutover. `scripts/hilt-supervisor.sh` and the generated LaunchAgent plist now carry the daemon flag by default; supervisor restart/adoption now refuses to preserve an old ws-server child when Granola is expected but its heartbeat is missing/stale; `npm run supervisor:status` reports the Granola heartbeat alongside the supervisor heartbeat; and `scripts/granola-sync.ts` loads `.env` so CLI status agrees with the running app.

- **Supervisor v1 post-verification fixes (6-agent workflow findings)** — The verification workflow (T1 unit gate, T2 API semantics, T4 fault injection, T5 lifecycle — all on scratch instances — plus adversarial spec and docs review) confirmed the core protocol (4 acceptance criteria VERIFIED pre-cutover) and surfaced real issues, all fixed: **(1) stamp-watcher defer bug** — a rebuild stamp written by a switch's own `npm run rebuild` was deferred (not ignored) while the transition ran, so the freshly-swapped server got killed and restarted once more the moment the switch finished; the watcher now absorbs in-transition stamps AND the switch syncs the watermark right when its build completes (closing the fast-swap race). **(2) Wedged-server detection** — the health loop only checked pid-liveness, so a hung-but-alive app-server on a headless machine would never self-recover; appServer now gets HTTP-probed each tick (90s post-spawn grace for slow dev compiles; ~4 consecutive failures ⇒ kill + backoff respawn). **(3) Root cause of the recurring :3000 breakage found** (three agents independently dated the damage to `npm run rebuild` starts): `next build` with `HILT_DIST_DIR=.next-prod` still rewrites/deletes parts of the default `.next/dev` — killing any RUNNING `next dev` on the same checkout (`required-server-files.json` ENOENT, all routes 500). Documented as an accepted same-checkout constraint in ARCHITECTURE §7 along with Next's dev-server singleton lock (supervisor dev mode auto-reverts if another next-dev runs); both vanish post-cutover when the supervisor owns the machine's only server. **(4)** Dead `delay` binding removed; **(5)** `HILT_SUPERVISOR_CHILDREN`/`HILT_SUPERVISOR_PORT` scratch knobs (shipped un-changelogged in ac5b854) documented.

### Added

- **Supervisor v1 — headless server lifecycle + remote dev/prod switch** (`docs/plans/supervisor-v1.md`, both phases) — The mode switch shipped earlier today only worked for the window's own Electron-spawned server; the user's real topology is "Mercury window → Mini server," so the switch had to travel to the serving machine. **Phase 1 (protocol):** the supervisor role is now a file protocol under `${DATA_DIR}` (`server/server-mode.ts`, ONE implementation shared by Electron, the daemon, and the Next reporting route): a 30s **heartbeat** (`app-supervisor.json`; `supervised` is honest — ≤90s + live pid, checked by `GET /api/system/app-server`), a **switch intent** (`app-mode-intent.json`, ts-deduped, written by new `POST /api/system/app-mode` — 202/409/400; tailnet-reachable by design, see ARCHITECTURE §7), and the existing mode/children state files. SourceToggle's switch section now renders **wherever the serving machine reports a live supervisor — local or remote source alike** — and switches over HTTP: POST, poll the self-report (supervisor `state`/`detail` stream into the popover), reload the window when `mode` flips (a swap changes the client bundle; remote viewers must reload themselves). The Electron-IPC switch path (`app-mode:*` handlers, preload `appMode` API) is **removed** — exactly one mechanism; Electron main now consumes the shared module, beats the heartbeat while it owns children, and acts on the same intent file. `electron/tsconfig.json` widened (rootDir `..`) so electron and the daemon literally compile the same file. **Phase 2 (daemon):** `server/supervisor.ts` + `com.hilt.supervisor` KeepAlive LaunchAgent (`npm run supervisor:run|install|uninstall|status`, `scripts/supervisor-launchd.ts`, wrapper `scripts/hilt-supervisor.sh` with the launcher's PATH discipline — launchd's minimal env is the same trap that broke Mercury) owns app-server/ws-server/event-server with capped-backoff restarts, **re-adopts** still-healthy children after a supervisor crash via the pid record, **stands by** when an external healthy Hilt owns the port (installable beside a running `dev:all`, claims on its exit), ignores rebuild stamps in dev mode, and a **dev TTL** (default 12h) returns a forgotten dev switch to prod. Unit tests: `npm run test:server-mode` (mode precedence, prod-build gating, spawn specs, intent dedupe shape, heartbeat freshness incl. dead-pid rejection).

### Fixed

- **`/navigate` rejected the Library view** — the ws-server's navigate allowlist predated the Library view (`{"view":"library"}` → 400). Found while driving Mercury's window remotely during the launch-hang investigation. Added `library` to the list.

- **Mercury launch hang: stale `/usr/local/bin/node` shadowed the launcher's modern Node for spawned servers** — On Mercury, launching `dist/Hilt.app` showed no window for 1–2 minutes. Root cause chain: Electron main's `childEnv()` hardcoded `/opt/homebrew/bin:/usr/local/bin` AHEAD of the inherited PATH; Mercury has no Homebrew node but does have a stale v18.13 at `/usr/local/bin/node`, so every spawned `npm run dev/start` (tsx → esbuild) crashed instantly with `TransformError`, `waitForServer` burned its full 60s timeout, and the window only appeared after fallback to the remote source — masking that Mercury's local server has likely been broken this way for a while. Fix in two layers: `CHILD_PATH` now puts the **inherited PATH first** (the `.app` launcher curates it, including an nvm prepend that picks v22 on Mercury) with the hardcoded dirs demoted to fallbacks for minimal Finder environments; and the launcher orders **Homebrew before `/usr/local`** (Apple Silicon convention — `/usr/local/bin/node` is often an old Intel-era installer leftover). Xochipilli unaffected by the reorder (launcher hands children Homebrew's v26 first, matching the ABI its `node_modules` were built with). Known follow-up worth doing: create the window (with the startup loading screen) BEFORE waiting on server spawns, so a slow/failed server narrates progress instead of presenting a dead dock icon.

### Added

- **In-app dev/prod mode switch + server-mode badge (SourceToggle)** — Follow-on to the prod-mode daily driver, for the rapid-iteration use case: "sometimes I want to switch to dev mode because I'm OK with the app being slower — I want to see my changes as real time as possible," without the re-create-the-app song and dance. **Mode is now runtime state**: `${DATA_DIR}/app-mode.json` (the UI's durable choice) wins over the launcher-baked `HILT_APP_MODE` (now just the fresh-install default; `npm run app` and `app:prod` create the same bundle). **Visibility**: every server self-reports via new `GET /api/system/app-server` (`mode` / `build_id` / `built_at`, with the rebuild stamp preferred over mid-build BUILD_ID for an honest age) — the SourceToggle dropdown badges the active source (`dev` amber / `prod · 2h`), and the same `AppServerInfo` rides the System machine identity payload (`SystemMachine.app_server`) so peer machines report theirs. **The switch**: when Electron supervises the server (spawned it, vs attached to a terminal server — `hasOwnedServers()`), a "Server mode" section in the dropdown switches over IPC (`app-mode:get/switch/status` via the preload bridge). To dev: kill + respawn on the same port (~5–15s incl. first compile), reload. To prod: **rebuild first while the current server keeps serving** (~30s, status streamed to the popover), then a ~1s swap — after a dev session the prod build is stale by definition, so the build is always part of the return trip. **Reliability**: single-flight guard shared with the rebuild watcher; if the new mode's server fails to come up, Electron auto-reverts to the previous mode (the window never dies); a rebuild stamp landing while in dev mode is ignored (picked up on the next switch to prod); attached-server and plain-browser topologies show honest read-only states. Verified live on both modes (badge + route self-report on dev :3000 and a `.next-prod` prod instance); the full IPC switch path gets its first exercise in the running Electron app.

- **Production-mode daily driver: `npm run app:prod` + `npm run rebuild`** — The daily-driver `dist/Hilt.app` has been running the dev server all day: React development mode (~2x slower rendering, double-invoked effects), unminified bundles, on-demand route compilation. New prod mode keeps the same uncompiled-web-app workflow but serves a real production build. `npm run app:prod` builds Next into **`.next-prod`** (its own dist dir via the existing `HILT_DIST_DIR` hook, so it never fights a dev server over `.next`) and creates the same `dist/Hilt.app` with `HILT_APP_MODE=prod` baked into the launcher (`create-dev-app.sh` placeholder, same pattern as the project-dir bake). The tweak loop is **`npm run rebuild` (~30s)**: build + touch `.next-prod/.hilt-rebuild-stamp` as the build-complete signal (BUILD_ID is written mid-build and can't be trusted). The running Electron main watches the stamp, restarts only its **owned** Next.js children on their existing ports, and reloads the window — the Electron wrapper itself never restarts. Spawn paths factored into `spawnSourceServerProcess`/`spawnPrimaryServerProcess` (shared by startup and rebuild-restart, with close-handler identity guards so a stale exit event can't clobber the replacement child); multi-source setups restart per-source on their own ports; prod requested without a build falls back to dev with a warning. Composes with the gateway app-server work: prod mode spawns `npm run start -- --port N` → production `server/app-server.ts` (which honors `--port`/`HILT_DIST_DIR` and hosts the single-origin `/events` upgrade) — verified live against the `.next-prod` build. `npm run app` (dev mode, hot reload) is unchanged for hacking on Hilt itself. Caveat in ARCHITECTURE §7: prod builds inline the `next.config.ts` env flags (graph/semantic) at build time — flag flips need a rebuild, not just a relaunch.

### Changed
